Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                        HARRIS
EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
The Klaipeda Harbour entrance will be improved by the construction of two new breakwaters to
extent the existing breakwaters, by the rehabilitation of the two existing breakwaters and by
deepening and widening the entrance channel and a part of the harbour basin to - 14 meters.
The sediments to be dredged under this project     various htpes of soils of which a nart
is contaminated. Of these sediments, all clean sands will be beneficially used. The
contaminated sediments would need to be dredged separately and stored in a confined disposal
facility. However, no such facility yet exists. The remaining clean glacial till and silty sediments
will be dumped at a designated disposal site about 20 kilometres offshore from Klaipeda. The
project and its impacts on the environment are extensively described in the Environment Impact
Assessment Report of the project, the executive summary of which is presented below.
BACKGROUND
When in 1991 the independence of Lithuania was restored, the idea of creating a united,
modern and universal seaport was promoted. Since that date, the structure of Klaipeda Port has
been fundamentally reorganised and the port activities are now legislated by the Klaipeda Port
Act. The Klaipeda State Seaport Authority (KSSA) is in charge of the functioning of the Port and
is responsible for maintenance, reconstruction and modernisation of the Port infrastructure,
while separate independent terminals are managing operations.
In 1997, as part of "the Programme of Construction and reconstruction of infrastructure objects
of Klaipeda State Seaport up to the year 2000", some 25 million USD were invested in the port
infrastructure. The navigational channel was deepened and at present ships with draft of up to
10.5 m can enter the Port.
In 1996, as part of the overall plan and with the aim of increasing safety and reducing downtime
the KSSA requested Delft Hydraulics of the Netherlands to carry out a study on alternative
improvements to the sea entrance. The study included the evaluation of the design layouts on
the basis of a series of full mission simulations by the Maritime Simulation Centre of the
Netherlands in co-operation with Delft Hydraulics. This feasibility study provided the basis for a
new design, which included i.a. the construction of new breakwaters, deepening and widening
of the access channel and re-alignment of the axis of the inner harbour channel.
In 1997, KSSA requested the Lithuanian Energy Institute to carry out a technical study on the
proposed dredging works. This study provided the basis for the design of the dredging works
and the potential impact on the environment. It also addressed the impact of the dredging works
on the stability of the existing breakwaters.
In 1998, the KSSA commissioned Frederic R. Harris in association with EDC - Environmental &
Dredging Consultancy and Uostamiescio projektas, to prepare the final design for the Klaipeda
Port Entrance rehabilitation, including the final design of the new breakwaters and the dredging
works, as well as this Environmental Impact Assessment.
The main purpose of the port entrance rehabilitation is to reduce wave penetration into the port
and give larger vessels improved and safe access to the port. The project is co-ordinated by
World Bank. The design works are financed by a grant from Netherlands and Japanese
Governments.
H7371   Draft Final Environmental Impact Assessment   1                        September 1999
Executive Summary



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                        HARRIS
NEED FOR REHABILITATION
The Port of Klaipeda is the main port of Lithuania. It is located on the south-east coast of the
Baltic Sea at the entrance of the Curonian lagoon. Particularly during the winter months, under
rough weather conditions, navigation through the entrance channel is dangerous and the deep
water berths at the oil port and the Klasco Port are unusable.
in the recent past a number of accidents occurred with shins runnina out of control at the
entrance of Klaipeda Port. Over the last 15 years four major accidents occurred. In two of these
cases the ship was wrecked and in one case there was major damage to a quay and cranes.
One of the accidents involved a tanker and resulted in a large oil spill. Taking the traffic volume
into consideration four major accidents in such a short period is clearly too much.
Especially entering or departing of loaded vessels of 20,000 DWT and more, compose a source
of potential danger. These ships must follow the relatively narrow channel and negotiate an
abrupt 230 bend, not wider than the channel itself and located directly at the entrance. When
inbound this leads to relatively high speeds in order to be able to compensate for wind, waves
and current while sailing within the channel limits. Slowing down or stopping occurs relatively
close to the oil terminals.
Under severe weather conditions the length of the breakwaters provides insufficient protection
against waves to the tugs to allow them to assist these vessels should assistance be required.
If tankers must leave the oil terminals under emergency conditions, only a relatively small
distance is available to accelerate to a sufficiently high speed and an adequate course to depart
safely from the sheltered harbour area.
From the above it can be concluded that in its present state the nautical safety of the port is
below any international standard. In addition it is to be noted that the harbour's breakwaters
(especially the Southern one) have sustained damage during recent storms and possible further
damage would enhance the problems just mentioned.
ALTERNATIVES EVALUATED UNDER THIS EIA
Three alternatives were considered under this EIA to address the need for rehabilitation.
Alternative 1: No-Action
In this alternative the present situation will remain unchanged. The proposed project will not be
executed, which means no dredging and construction activities will be carried out. This
alternative is taken as the "neutral" reference for comparison of the other two alternatives.
Alternative 2: The proposed (original) project
This alternative includes the construction of two new breakwaters and dredging of
approximately 2 million m3 of sand, silt and glacial till sediments. In this project alternative, all
dredged sands (from the outer entrance channel) will be beneficially used for nearshore or
beach replenishment. All silty sediments as well as all the glacial till sediments will be disposed
off at the designated offshore disposal site. In this alternative all non sand sediments will be
dredged as one volume, which means that no differentiation will be made between clean and
contaminated sediments and between silty sand and glacial till.
Alternative 3: The proposed project plus confined disposal facility
This alternative is the same as the proposed project, but with some changes in the execution of
the dredging works. In this alternative the contaminated sediments will be dredged separately
from the clean sediments and subsequently stored in a confined disposal facility (CDF). With
respect to the CDF it is to be noted that the feasibility, the design characteristics and the
H7371   Draft Final Environmental Impact Assessment   2                        September 1999
Executive Summary



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                        HARIS
location for implementation are still to be worked out. Some initial studies have been carried in
this respect.
Dredging of the contaminated sediments will be done in line with modern practice of removing
contaminated sediments, i.e. with high dredging accuracy, minimal turbidity and resuspension of
contaminated sediments and minimal spill.
PROPOSED ACTION
Each alternative was evaluated on a number of criteria both for the construction period and the
subsequent operational phase, and compliance with international environmental regulations.
Although the proposed project (alternative 2) already has a significant positive environmental
impact by reducing navigation hazards and consequently oil pollution risks at the Klaipeda port,
the planned offshore disposal of contaminated sediments is considered to be a violation of
international environmental agreements.
Consequently, alternative 3 has been selected as the Preferred alternative and Proposed
Action. This alternative will require the implementation of a CDF. The CDF, which can be
constructed from uncontaminated dredged materials (Glacial till), should be designed to solve
not only the contaminated sediment problem from this project, but also to provide a solution for
other contaminated sediment problems elsewhere in the port areas. Details on contaminated
sediments elsewhere in the port are given in the main text.
Environmental information used to produce this document results from numerous studies and
field surveys by several agencies and investigators working in the study area over the past
several years. Especially the contributions of the experts of the Klaipeda University were
extremely useful. The summary of the data and interpretations presented are a synthesis of all
available information found to be recent, accurate, and applicable to the evaluations.
PUBLIC PARTICIPATION
An opportunity to review the draft version of the EIA (in the Lithuanian language) was
announced twice in the local Klaipeda newspaper. Public response was limited and the Port
Authorities received no formal comments on the EIA by December 31, 1998.
In December 1998, copies of the draft EIA have been presented to the Lithuanian Ministry of the
Environment, the Klaipeda Municipality, the Klaipeda County Governor's Administration, the
Klaipeda public health centre of the Ministry of Health, the fire-fighting department of the
Ministry of Home Affairs, the Project Expertise Bureau, the KSSA and to representatives of the
World Bank, for review. By June 1999 only comments from the Worldbank representatives had
been received.
A technical public hearing was organised by the Port Authorities on May 11, 1999. The
discussions focussed on the costs of the breakwaters, the direct benefits of the works for
Lithuanian contractors and the width of the harbour opening.
A public hearing on the environmental aspects of the project and the resulting EIA was
organised by the Port Authorities on September 15, 1999. During the meeting serious concerns
were expressed by the participants in relation to the delay in implementing a Confined Disposal
Facility for safe storage of contaminated sediments and regarding the damage of offshore
dumping of dredged sediments on fisheries. The findings of the public hearings have been
included in the EIA.
ALTERNATIVE ANALYSIS
The impact assessments and use-conflict criteria were divided into two groups, those related to
the construction activities during the project and those related to the subsequent operations at
H7371   Draft Final Environmental Impact Assessment   3                        September 1999
Executive Summary



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                           HARRIS
the rehabilitated port entrance. The evaluation of each alternative included the consideration of
all possible detrimental, mitigatable, or beneficial impacts that could result from implementation
of the alternatives. The following information summarises the pros and cons resulting from this
analysis.
Major positive effects are expected in relation to navigational conditions and safety, and the
related reduction of oil spill risks. The new breakwaters will also have a small positive effect on
fisheries and aquatic life in the proJiet area
The project is expected to result in higher future maintenance costs and will have a negative
effect on water quality in the Baltic Sea if contaminated sediments are dumped at the offshore
disposal site.
During construction several detrimental effects are to be expected. However, as all of these
effects are related to the construction and dredging activities they are all of a temporary nature.
This means they will stop once the project is finished. Included in these temporary effects are
detrimental effects on water quality, aquatic life, especially if contaminated sediments are
dredged without precautions. Small detrimental effects are expected in relation to fisheries,
navigation.(hindrance) and urban land traffic. Mitigating measures to minimise the indicated
negative effects are presented in this report.

Executive Summary



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                        HARRIS
PREFERED ALTERNATIVE
Alternative 3 has been selected as the so-called Preferred Alternative and was presented
accordingly to the Port Authorities in the draft EIA (September 1998). This alternative was found
to have the same benefits as alternative 2, but the least and less severe negative impacts, while
still meeting the goal of the Client, e.g. a safer and more economic port.
ENCROACHEMENT ON PREFERRED ALTERNATIVE AND PROPOSED ACTION
During the execution of the EIA study for the project, upon KSSA's initiative the area to be
dredged under this project was split into two tenders. One tender organised by Frederic R. Harris
(FRH) and financed by a World Bank loan, covering the (re)construction of the breakwaters and
the dredging (practically) from the existing coastline seawards. The other tender organised by the
Lithuanian Energy Institute (LEI) and financed by KSSA itself, covering the dredging from the
existing coastline land inwards. The dredging area under the FRH tender comprises only clean
sediments, whereas practically all surface sediments under the LEI tender can be classified as
contaminated under the Lithuanian classification system.
In view of the fact that a CDF had not yet been implemented, the KSSA requested permission
from the Lithuanian Ministry of the Environment to be allowed to dump the contaminated
sediments present in the dredging area covered under the LEI tender at sea. Although not in line
with the concept of environmental protection, or the international attempts to improve the water
quality of the Baltic Sea - measures to improve the water quality in and around Klaipeda are listed
as priority actions under the Baltic Sea Programme approved by the regional Ministers of
Environment at Helsinki (April 1992) and Gdansk (March 1993) - this permission was granted and
early 1999 dredging in the LEI area started. During the summer of 1999 practically all
contaminated and clean sediments had been dredged in the LEI dredging area and had been
dumped offshore.
Consequently, with no contaminated sediments present in the dredging area covered under the
FRH tender and all the contaminated sediments already removed from the LEI dredging area, the
so-called preferred alternative as developed in this EIA appears no longer relevant for this
project.
However, there is still a considerable volume of contaminated sediments left in various parts of
the Klaipeda port. Lithuanian experts estimate the present volume of class 3 and 4 sediments at
approximately 200.000 m3. Undoubtedly, more contaminated sediments will be formed
(deposited) in enclosed port areas in the years ahead. This clearly demonstrates that the
implementation of a CDF is still very relevant.
According the Minister of Transport and Communications, Mr. R. Didziokas, the project for
storage of contaminated sediments will form part of the Public Investment programme and the
Tina programme as a separate project. The implementation of this project is anticipated in 2001.
ENVIRONMENTAL MANAGEMENT PLAN
As the project will influence a variety of environmental and social aspects, an Environmental
Management Plan (EMP) has been included in the EIA. This EMP contains a review of the
anticipated adverse effects, defines adequate measures to mitigate them, and establishes a
monitoring program to measure and control both the impacts and the effectiveness of the
mitigating measures.

1   INTRODUCTION
In May 1998 the Klaipeda State Seaport Authority commissioned Frederic R. Harris B.V. in
association with EDC - Environmental & Dredging Consultancy and Uostamiescio projektas, the
design of the Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation project. This design includes the preparation
of tender documents for the construction of two new breakwaters and the rehabiiitation of the
existing breakwaters, the dredging works for the deepening of the entrance channel and harbour
basin, the improvement of the mooring/fendering at the Oil and Klasco berths and the installation
of a wave/current measuring device near the harbour entrance to support the pilotage.
Although the proposed project should have a significant positive environmental impact by
reducing navigation hazards and consequently oil pollution risks at the Klaipeda Port, the
proposed project has been placed in environmental screening category "A", according World
Bank regulations. This in view of potential for serious environmental impacts associated with the
construction of the new breakwaters, the volume of the proposed dredging works (> 1,000,000 m3
of partly contaminated sediment), and the presence of fish spawning places and fish migrating
routes in the project area.
This report presents the results of the Environmental Impact Assessment, which was carried out
according the requirements of the World Bank's Operational Directive OP/BP 4.01. The content of
this report has been written in such a manner, that most can be read without specific knowledge
of the relevant fields of expertise.
This EIA was prepared in the period May 1998 to September 1999. Its contents is based on the
information available at that time.
The consultants acknowledge the co-operation they received from the Klaipeda State Seaport
Authorities, the Lighthouse and Hydrografical Service, specialists from the Baltic Eco Association
and from Mr. Pedro Taborga, Mr. Inesis Kiskis and Mr. Piotr Krzyzanowski from the World Bank.
Also they gratefully acknowledge the assistance they received from experts of the Klaipeda
University and Dr. Arturas Razinkovas and Dr. Sergej Olenin in particular, Dr. Kestutis Joksas of
the Lithuanian Institute of Geology, Prof. Brunonas Gailiusis of the Lithuanian Energy Institute and
Arturas Slauteris of Geoprojektas.
Drs. Ronald W. van Oostrum (EDC) was the principal environmental specialist responsible for the
preparation of this EIA. Ir. Cock van der Lem is the Harris project manager for this contract. Ir.
Rudy Broekens and Ir. Pieter Janssen were responsible for production of this report.
The report has been structured as follows:
In chapter 2 the legal and administrative framework is given. This section includes the relevant
environmental laws and regulations, as well as information on the cummunity involvement and
public hearings.
A description of the project is given in chapter 3. This chapter also describes the method of
construction of the new breakwaters as well as the possible dredging scenarios.
Chapter 4 deals with the baseline data on the present situation and is divided into seven sections
related to: general information on the study area, climate, hydraulics, geology, topography and
sediment characteristics, water characteristics, ecological characteristics and special features of
the study area.
The environmental impact of the project during operation is presented in chapter 5. A
differentiation is made between impacts on hydraulics, wave climate inside the port,
H7371   Draft Final Environmental impact Assessment   1-a                        September 1999



-- s   Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                            HARRIS
sedimentation and erosion processes, salt intrusion into the lagoon, navigational conditions,
environmental risks, aquatic life and fisheries.
The environmental impact of the project during construction is presented in chapter 6. Here the
effects of the dredging and disposal activities, as well as the construction of the new breakwaters
are reviewed. A differentiation is made between impacts of dredging and disposal and breakwater
construction on water quality, aquatic life and fisheries. In addition the impact of dredginq on the
stability of the existing breakwaters, the impact on maritime and land traffic and the impact on
recreation is reviewed.
In chapter 7 options for beneficial use of the dredged sediments and options for an
environmentally sound approach to the problem of contaminated sediments are given. In addition
the environmental aspects of three alternative project policies (no action, proposed project, more
environmental friendly alternative) are reviewed and evaluated.
In chapter 8 the environmental management program (EMP) is presented. This EMP includes a
review of the most significant environmental effects, defines adequate measures to mitigate them,
and establishes a monitoring program to control both the impacts and the effectiveness of the
mitigating measures.
An executive summary is given at the beginning of this report.

2   LEGAL AND ADMINISTRATIVE FRAMEWORK
International guidelines and national legislation enforce environmental protection in Lithuania.
Accordind to the governmental resolution No 456 of 12 May 1997, the proposed project belongs to
the category of economical activities and objects, which requires a comprehensive Environmental
Impact Assessment to be made. The following review summarises the laws and regulations
applicable to this specific project.
2.1    LITHUANIAN ENVIRONMENTAL REGULATIONS
LAW ON ENVIRONMENT PROTECTION OF THE REPUBLIC OF LITHUANIA OF 1992 AND AMENDMENTS AND
SUPPLEMENTS TO THIS LAW OF 28 MAY 1996
This law states the functions of the Ministry of Environment, municipal institutions in the field of
environment protection, the obligations of governmental, management and control institutions
assuring the rights of citizens and public organisations (Article 8).
The economic activities are planned and executed following this and other laws, by-laws, legal
acts, programs for environment protection and environmental monitoring, general and master
plans and projects, evaluating the potential of environment protection of the Republic of Lithuania
(Chapter 15).
Legal and physical persons who are planning to start economic activities must make an
Environmental Impact Assessment according to the laws existing in Lithuania. This must be done
on their own account and the results must be handed for approval to a number of institutions
according to the list confirmed by the Government of Lithuania. Those institutions evaluate the
handed document about the possible impact on environment and according to their competence
give their conclusions or motivated review concerning the possibility of such activity. The review is
compulsory for the institution, which issues licences for economic activity (Article 15).
LAw ON ENVIRONMENTAL IMPACT ASSESSMENT OF THE REPUBLIC OF L1THUANIA ADOPTED ON AUGUST
15, 1996
This law regulates the environmental impact assessment and the relationship of the participants
of this process (Article 2).
According article 6, the participants of the environmental impact assessment process are:
1) Reievant parties of the environment impact assessment of a proposed activity, being:
Proponents of the proposed activity and organisations of physical planning; Ministry of
Environment; Ministry of Health; Fire-fighting department; County governor's institution; Municipal
institution (see Table 2-1).
2) Public (Society)
Resolutions of the Government of Lithuania and orders of the Ministry of Environment related to
this law include:
*  The Governmental Resolution No 456 of 12 May 1997 by the Government of the Republic of
Lithuania, which indicates the types of activities and objects where the comprehensive
environment impact assessment is to be made. These include ports (all cases) and dredging
of water territory (all cases).
*  The order No 170 of the Ministry of Environment of 18 September 1997. The order is fixed for
the documents for the planning of the territory, decisions and consequences and reports on
Environment Impact Assessment that are analysed in the Ministry of Environment. In this
H7371   Draft Final Environmental Impact Assessment   2-1                      September 1999

Environment Impact Assessment program, and distribution of functions of the services.
* The order No 49 of 19 March 1998 by the Ministry of Environment of the Republic of

the evaluation of Environment Impact Assessment.
* The Governmental Resolution No 1305 of 11 November 1996 of the Government of the

* Initial environment impact assessment - when the documents for the planning of the territory
are prepared and detailed plans are prepared,
* Comprehensive environment impact assessment is to be made - when the technical project is

types of economic activities and objects the list of which is confirmed by the decree No 873 of the

the Ministry of Environment.

information and give proposals, remarks as well as claims. Municipalities organise the
participation of the society in the process. Public discussion is to be organised by the Employer on

LAW ON WATER TERRITORY OF THE REPUBLIC OF LITHUANIA OF 1997
This law foresees that dredging and cleaning works of the bottom for navigational needs are to be
executed according to the regulations approved by the Ministry of Environment (Article 19).
THE LAW OF THE MARINE ENVIRONMENT PROTECTION OF 1997
This law foresees that it is necessary to apply the requirements of the marine environmental
protection from contaminated materials for the planned economic activity in the way that is set in
the Annex I of Helsinki Convention (Article 6).
The limitations for disposal of the dredged ground are not applied on condition that the disposal is
executed in inland or territorial waters with the permission of the Ministry of Environment (Article
28).
Article 48 foresees that the economic activity that might have negative impact on the marine
environment can be executed only by the order fixed by the laws on environment protection,
environment impact assessment for planned economic activities, i.e. when a positive decision
from the Ministry of Environment is received.
ADDITIONAL DREDGING RELATED RULES
In addition to these laws "The temporary rules for the dredging of water territory of Klaipeda Port,
entrance channel and dumping of the soil at sea" are valid, according the approved order No 54 of
the Ministry of Environment of 16 November 1994.
In the order No 67 of 17 April 1997 by the Minister of the Environment called "Concerning the
evaluation of loss made to fishery due to dredging works in the port", it is determined that the
dredging of water territory of the port during fish migration can be executed only when it is
extremely necessary and fixed conditions are to be fulfilled (from April 1 to May 31 and from
August 16 to October 31).
The text of both dredging related rules is included as Appendix B to this report.
INTERNATIONAL CONVENTIONS
The Gdansk Convention
The Convention on Fishing and Conservation of the Living Resources in the Baltic Sea and the
Belts - the Gdansk Convention - was signed in September 1973 and entered into force in 1974.
The objectives of the Gdansk Convention are to achieve greater and closer co-operation between
the Parties in order to maintain the maximum stable productivity of the living resources of the
region.
The provisions of the convention are restricted to fishery aspects only. No reference is made
regarding pollution aspects or dredging works. Only the very general concept of "conservation of
the living resources" is considered relevant to the project. In this respect, protective measures for
fisheries during construction, dredging and disposal and the related scientific investigations
(monitoring programs) can be considered relevant issues under this convention.
The ESPO Convention:
The Convention on Environmental Impact Assessment in a Transboundary Context (Espoo, 1991)
stipulates the obligations of Parties to assess the environmental impact of certain activities at an
early stage of planning. It also lays down the general obligation of States to notify and consult
H7371   Draft Final Environmental Impact Assessment   2-3                      September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                         A
HARRIS
each other on all major projects under consideration that are likely to have a significant adverse
environmental impact across boundaries.
The list of activities relevant for this convention does not include port rehabilitation projects or
dredging works. As the proposed project is not expected to have significant adverse
environmental impact across the countries boundaries, this convention is considered to be not
applicable.
The Helsinki Convention:
The Seimas of the Republic of Lithuania on 12 March 1997 ratified the Helsinki Convention on
Marine Environmental Protection of the basin of the Baltic Sea of 1992.
The objectives of the Convention on the protection of the Marine Environment of the Baltic Sea
Area (1992 Helsinki Convention), are to take all appropriate measures, individually or by means of
regional operation, to prevent and eliminate pollution in order to promote the ecological restoration
ik         of the Baltic Sea area and the preservation of its ecological balance. The 1992 convention
succeeds the older 1974 convention on the protection of the marine environment of the Baltic Sea
areas.
The Convention stipulates in Article 11 "Prevention of dumping"', paragraph 2:
Dumping of dredged material shall be subject to a prior special permit issued by the appropriate
national authority in accordance with the provisions of Annex V. This especially the case with
disposal of contaminated sediments and as such relevant to the project area.
Furthermore Lithuania is party to the following international environmental agreements:
Biodiversity,  Climate  Change,  Ozone  Layer  Protection,  Ship  Pollution,  Wetlands

2.3  COMMUNITY INVOLVEMENT AND PUBLIC HEARINGS
2.3.1   Notification to the public
The draft EIA was presented to the KSSA in September 1998. After translation into the Lithuanian
language, this draft EIA was made available to the general public for review. The invitation by the
Port Authorities was published twice in the local Klaipeda newspaper, i.e. on October 19, 1998
and on November 4, 1998 (copies are included in appendix D). The number of people that came
to review the report was rather small (approximately 10) and no comments were received or
noted.
2.3.2  Public hearings
The people possibly affected by the works can be divided into two levels:
*  The directly involved or affected communities, which include fishermen, port operators,
people living near the beaches to be reclaimed, tourist facilities like hotels, people living or
working near the construction site.
*  The indirectly involved communities include those who, because of their particular concern or
expertise, may have relevant information regarding the nature, scope, and particulars of
potential environmental effects, e.g. consulting engineers and NGO's.
The indirect involved communities including many university lecturers have been involved from
the very beginning of the EIA preparations. Many of them have contributed to the contents of the
EIA report. See also appendix C: list of contributors.
In addition two public hearing were held at the KSSA office in Klaipeda. The first was related to
technical aspects of the project, whereas during the second one the environmental aspects of the
project and the resulting EIA was discussed.
Public hearing on technical aspects: May 11. 1999
In Spring 1999 in local newspapers in Klaipeda some articles were published where the authors
put into discussion whether a vertical breakwater would not be cheaper than the rubble mound
breakwater presented in the draft EIA report. Although it was quickly revealed that the calculations
in the newspapers included some calculation errors, the Klaipeda State Seaport Authority decided
to organise a meeting in Klaipeda in order to present and discuss the subject with people who had
expressed their interest. This meeting was organised on 11 May 1999 and was attended by the
authors of the articles (Lithuanian architects and engineers), representatives from the Lithuanian
Institute of Engineers, representatives of 'Expertise" bureau and several others (see below). On
behalf of the Consultants Mr. J.C. van der Lem was present.
At the start of the meeting, Mr. Van der Lem gave the attendees an overview of the project. First
of al the reason for the project was indicated. Further the results of the work done by Delft
Hydraulics and MARIN/MSCN in the previous studies to the project was presented and finally the
work done by the Consultants.
During the discussions after the presentation, comments and remarks were made with respect to:
1.     Costs of the breakwaters and comparison to vertical breakwater
2.     Direct benefit of the project to Lithuania
3.     Width of the harbour entrance
Ad 1.  Cost comparison
With respect to the cost comparison Consultants indicated that Delft Hydraulics in 1997/1998 had
made a cost comparison for rubble mound breakwaters and vertical breakwaters. This
comparison demonstrated that the rubble mound breakwater is less expensive than a vertical
breakwater. Verification of the rates by the Consultants at the start of the present project revealed
that indeed the vertical breakwater is more expensive than a rubble mound breakwater.
H7371   Draft Final Environmental Impact Assessment   2-5                        September 1999



Kiaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project
7                                                                     ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~HARPIS
In addition to this, Consultants emphasised that the primary objective of the project is to reduce
the wave conditions inside the port. Important aspect in this respect is the reflection of waves
against the breakwaters inside the port. Therefore a vertical breakwater is less favourable than a
rubble mound breakwater.
Finally, because of the importance of fish spawning, a rubble mound breakwater (with its high
porosity) is also to be preferred over the vertical (caisson) breakwater (with its rigid, closed fronts).
Ad 2.  Direct benefit of the project to Lithuania
During the discussions it became clear that attendees would prefer a vertical breakwater since
this would result in a higher direct benefit to Lithuania. Assuming the vertical breakwater to be of a
caisson type, it would need to be constructed locally. This would result in (more) use of local
labour as well as local construction materials, which would give a direct benefit to Lithuania and to
Klaipeda more particularly.
Although Consultants do not deny this, they do not consider the direct benefit to Lithuania an
argument to select a (more expensive) vertical breakwater. Also in the construction of the rubble
mound breakwaters local labour will be included. In case of construction of the rubble mound
breakwaters with tetrapods (as will be an option to the contractors) still a substantial amount of
local construction materials will be included in the project.
Finally, the implementation of the project will have a far larger (and lasting) effect on the economy
in Lithuanian than the mere construction itself.
Ad 3.  Width of the harbour entrance
The width of the entrance was discussed and again it was emphasised that a width of 150 m was
considered too small. Preferably a width of 300 m was to be taken, being the length of the vessels
entering the port.
Consultants emphasised that in Rotterdam the channel is in the order of 500 m width for vessels
up to 300,000 DWT (approx. 350 m length). However in Rotterdam the entrance channel is a dual
passage way, whereas in Klaipeda it is only a single passage way. Finally, Consultants explained
that it is still anticipated to execute additional ship simulation studies once results of
measurements with the new measurement system are obtained.
When the meeting was adjourned, no formal "agreement" had been reached in the sense that
some people kept their (personal) opinions and reservations. The KSSA is preparing the Minutes
of Meetings, which will be distributed to the attendees in due course.
The list of participants to this community meeting is presented in Appendix D.

t                                                                 ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~HARRIS
Public hearinq on the environmental aspects and the EIA: September 1 5, 1 999
In line with the EIA requirements, a public hearing on the project and its environmental aspects
was organised at the KSSA office on September 15.
The public was informed about and invited to participate by means of an add in the
Klaipeda Newspaper of September 6, 1999. In addition a letter of invitation was send to 7
NGO's. A project summary document was attached to the letter of invitation. Both the
newspaper invitation and the list of invited NGO's have been included in appendix D.
Approximately 30 participants were present at the hearing, which was also covered by local
television (broadcasted the same night) and local newspapers.
On behalf of the Consultants Mr. J.C. van der Lem (project manager) and Mr Ronald van Oostrum
(environmental specialist) were present.
After being introduced by Mr. Vitas Kaunas (project manager KSSA - PIU1, Mr. Van der Lem
gave the attendees an overview of the project. Subsequently, Mr. van Oostrum presented a
&          detailed review of the realisation of the EIA and of the environmental aspects of the works.
The comments and remarks made during the discussions after the presentations, as well as the
related answers, are summarised hereafter:
From Fisheries Research laboratorv
1. At present, dumping of dredged materials also takes place outside the designated
offshore disposal areas. As a consequence of decades of dumping a large sea area has
been negatively affected. In view of the damage done in this way to the fishing industry
some compensation might be justified. What is your opinion on that?
Replv: A specific dumping area has been indicated in the contract documents. If the
contractor complies with the requirement only to dump at this area, we do not think the
contractor should pay a compensation fee. Monitoring will be carried on to ensure that
dredged sediments are only dumped at the designated disposal site.
The topic of compensation in general (not specific for this project) is something that
might be discussed with the Ministry of the Environment.
2. The indicated disposal site for dredged sediments is more than 30 years old and
completely full. So how can you dump there?
Reolv: Based on the information available to the Worldbank study team, the disposal
area indicated is still operational. This site was also used in the first six months of this
year (1999) for disposal of the sediments dredged in the LEI dredging area. However,
this aspect will be checked with the Ministry of the Environment.
From Lithuanian Green Movement
3. It is indicated in the documentation that the net sediment transport along the coast is
practically null. How sure is it that indeed no coastline erosion will take place north or
south of the breakwaters?
Rep/Z: This problem has been studied in detail in the course of the project. The experts
involved do not expect the breakwaters to have a noticeable effect on coastline
development. However, in view of the importance of this aspect, a monitoring program
has been identified to study coastline development and to verify the expert's
assumptions.
4. It is indicated in the documentation that contaminated sediments in the LEI part have
been dumped at sea with the approval of the Ministry of the Environment. As these
H7371   Draft Final Environmental Impact Assessment   2-7                     September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                      9
1                                                                                      HARRIS
sediments fall under the scope of the EIA, is it indicated in the EIA that these sediments
have caused damage to the marine environment?
Reoly: This aspect is clearly indicated in the main text of the EIA as well as in the
Executive Summary. It is acknowledged that the disposal of the contaminated
sediments will have caused damage to the marine environment. However, no specific
damage assessment has been carried nut in relation to the d.isposal of contaminatedl
sediments originating from the LEI dredging area. The main reasons being that:
1. Also from other parts of the port (including the highly contaminated Malku bay)
contaminated sediments have been dredged and dumped at the offshore disposal
site in the same period (1999).
2. Contaminated sediments have been dumped at the designated offshore disposal site
for many years.
Consequently, it is considered to be practically impossible to assess the damage caused
by the disposal of the contaminated sediments from the LEI area.
5. The development / implementation of a CDF has been planned for more than 5 years
now, but has been postponed twice. Will the CDF be implemented as part of the
present Worldbank project?
Reply: There is a clear desire from the side of the Worldbank to assist the Port
Authorities in solving the contaminated sediment problems of the Klaipeda port. Both
the Worldbank and the Port Authorities acknowledge that on short notice a solution in
the form of a CDF is in the Ports own interest. Within the present Worldbank dredging
area, no contaminated sediments are present. However contaminated sediments (class
3 and 4) are present practically everywhere along the seven kilometres long stretch of
the east bank of the Klaipeda Strait between the Winter Port to Malku Bay. This means
that any development in this area (dredging works or reconstruction of quay walls) will
involve handling of contaminated sediments.
6. Is money available for the implementation of a CDF?
Reply: This is still a point of discussion. No money has yet been allocated by the Port
Authorities for implementation of a CDF. The Worldbank is actively searching for
funding in this respect.
7. What are the rights of the public with respect to this project and the EIA? Is it possible
to oppose the project if it does not include a CDF?
Replv: By means of this public hearing, participants (the public and NGO's) can actively
participate in the EIA process. Concerns and comments by the public regarding the
project will be taken seriously and will be noted in the EIA. However, the function of the
EIA is limited to presenting and evaluating the pro's and con's for the natural and social
environment. It is up to the Ministry of the Environment and the Worldbank to accept or
reject the project or to decide to include a CDF. So, the rights of the participants of this
public hearing are limited in this respect.
8. What will be the maintenance costs of a CDF?
Reply: This costs for maintenance and after-care of a CDF will greatly depend on the
design, the size and the location of the CDF. As these aspects are part of an ongoing
investigation by the Worldbank team, no direct numbers can yet be given.

3   DESCRIPTION OF THE PROPOSED PROJECT
BACKGROUND OF THE PROJECT
When in 1991 the independence of Lithuania was restored, the idea of creating a united, modern
and universal seaport was promoted. Since that date, the structure of Kiaipeda Port has been
fundamentally reorganised and the port activities are now legislated by the Klaipeda Port Act.
The land and the infrastructure of the port are still state-owned, but the superstructures can be
privatised. The Klaipeda State Seaport Authority (KSSA) is in charge of the functioning of the
Port and the integration of it into Lithuanian transport complex. The KSSA is responsible for
maintenance, reconstruction and modernisation of the Port infrastructure, while separate
independent terminals are managing operations.
The Government of the Republic of Lithuania has approved a major investment program called
'the Programme of Construction and reconstruction of infrastructure objects of Klaipeda State
Seaport up to the year 2000". This programme includes the following projects:
1. Harbour entrance rehabilitation.
2. Dredging of the navigation channel and the harbour.
3. Container terminal.
4. Improvements of the Ro-Ro terminal.
5. Specialised quay for fertilisers and cement.
6. Specialised quays for scrap metal, timber, building materials.
7. Reconstruction of the quays.
8. Reconstruction of the railway interfaces.
9. Disposal site for contaminated sediments.
10. Passenger ferry terminal.
11. Cruise vessel terminal.
In 1997 some 25 million USD were invested in the port infrastructure. The navigational channel
was deepened and at present ships with draft of up to 10.5 m can enter the Port.
In 1996, as part of the overall plan and with the aim of increasing safety and reducing downtime
the KSSA requested Delft Hydraulics of the Netherlands to carry out a study on alternative
improvements to the sea entrance. The study included the evaluation of the design layouts on
the basis of a series of full mission simulations by the Maritime Simulation Centre of the
Netherlands in co-operation with Delft Hydraulics. This feasibility study provided the basis for a
new design, which included i.a. the construction of new breakwaters, deepening and widening of
the access channel and re-alignment of the axis of the inner harbour channel.
In 1997, KSSA requested the Lithuanian Energy Institute (LEI) to carry out a technical study on
the proposed dredging works. This study provided the basis for the design of the dredging works
and the potential impact on the environment. It also addressed the impact of the dredging works
on the stability of the existing breakwaters.
In 1998, the KSSA commissioned Frederic R. Harris B.V. in association with EDC -
Environmental & Dredging Consultancy and Uostamiescio Projektas, to prepare the final design
for the Klaipeda Port Entrance rehabilitation, including the final design of the new breakwaters
and the dredging works, as well as this Environmental Impact Assessment.
The main purpose of the port entrance rehabilitation is to reduce wave penetration into the port
and give larger vessels improved and safe access to the port. The project is co-ordinated by the
H7371   Draft Final Environmental Impact Assessment   3-1                      September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                        m
HARRIS
World Bank. The design works are financed by a grant from the Netherlands and Japanese
Governments.
3.1  GENERAL DESCRIPTION OF THE PROPOSED PROJECT
3.1 1  Improvement of Klaineda harbour entrance
The "Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Projecf' comprises:
 the construction of two new breakwaters to extend the existing breakwaters,
* the rehabilitation of the two existing breakwaters,
* dredging works for the deepening and widening of the access channel and deepening of a
part of the harbour basin to -14m, including the re-alignment of the inner harbour access
channel
* the improvement of the mooring/fendering at the Oil and KLASCO berths
*  the installation of a wave/current-measuring device near the harbour entrance to support the
pilotage.
Two of the above elements of the project are considered to be of relevance to the environmental
impact, i.e.: the construction of the two new breakwaters and the dredging and disposal works,
including the re-alignment of the navigational channel inside the port.
The main features of the works are shown in Figure 3-1. A summary of the basic characteristics
of these works is given in section 3.2 (method of construction).

3.1.2  Future options
In addition to the development plans for the Klaipeda port as described above, two plans need to
be mentioned, as they are of environmental importance:
ADDITIONAL DREDGING WORKS INSIDE THE PORT AREA
The presently proposed dredging works include the sea access channel and the northern
harbour area up to the Dane River. Based on the LEI dredging study (LEI 1997) it is clear, that
considerable additional deepening dredging works are being studied for the area from the Dane
River up to Alksnyne (some 5 kilometres in the direction of the lagoon). It is demonstrated in the
LEI study that the effect the present project will have on flow conditions in the Klaipeda Strait
and on salt intrusion into the lagoon may be increased considerably by additional deepening
dredging works in the remaining parts of the Klaipeda Port.
THE CONSTRUCTION OF A NEW DEEP-SEE HARBOUR OUTSIDE THE PRESENT PORT AREA
Recently studies have started regarding the feasibility of a new deep-sea port outside the
present port area in the Klaipeda Strait. The area considered for this new port is located directly
north of the existing north breakwater. That project is not expected to have any effect on the
environmental impacts of the present project.
3.2  METHOD OF CONSTRUCTION
3.2.1  Dredging and disposal works
DESIGN OF DREDGING WORKS
As indicated above (Background of the project), KSSA requested the Lithuanian Energy Institute
in 1997 to carry out a technical study on the proposed dredging works. This study provided the
basis for the design of the dredging works.
The original limits of the entire dredging area go from the 16 m. depth contour line in the Baltic
Sea up to the harbour entrance, the northern and southern breakwaters and the northern part of
the harbour area up to the mouth of the Dane River. The sediment quality investigations as
carried out by the LEI demonstrated that the most inner part of the project area (the first
kilometer from the Dane River seawards including the enclosed port area) contained severely
contaminated sediments. Based on these findings it was decided by KSSA not to dredge and
deepen this area for the time being. Subsequently this part was taken out of the dredging plans.
In March 1998, the KSSA commissioned Fred. R. Harris in association with EDC -
Environmental & Dredging Consultancy and Uostamiescio projektas, to prepare the final design
for the Klaipeda Port Entrance rehabilitation, including the final design of the dredging works.
There was a clear overlap in the works to be carried out in relation to the dredging part of the
project between the works of this World Bank team and the LEI. In order to prevent double work,
the Port Authorities decided to split the dredging area into two parts.
The dredging area was subdivided into 41 sections of varying size according to the scheme
given in Figure 3-2. The boundaries of the dredging area for the World Bank team are marked
by line 27 (between oil berth 2 and 3) and line 71 (out at sea).
H7371   Draft Final Environmental Impact Assessment   3-3                    September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                           m
HARRIS
Consequently the design characteristics of the total dredging works as presented in this report
are a mixture of the dredging design by the LEI (from the Dane River up to line 27) and the
dredging design by the World Bank team (from line 27 to the 16 m depth contour line).
The access channel has a design depth of 14 meters and a width of 150 meters (between the
toe-lines). Slopes are a design factor, which would in this shallow layer dredging not affect
volumes significantly. Slopes can be defined as: "box-cut equivalent of natural angle of repose";
boulder clayk will stand at any excavated angle including vertical, the sands would be expected to
settle in the order of 1 vertical to 5-8 horizontal.
Acceptable dredging tolerances are still to be discussed, but for calculation purposes a vertical
tolerance of 50 cm and a horizontal tolerance of 3 meters is assumed for this project. However
these tolerances may be minimised by proper equipment selection.

SEDIMENT CHARAcTERISTicS AND VOLUMES
The following description of the sediments, as well as the volumes involved are based on the
data as presented in the LEI report and soil investigations carried out by Consultants. Although
H7371   Draft Finai Environmental Impact Assessment    3-4                        September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabifitation Project                                          D
HARRIS
the final quantities of the various sediments to be dredged might to some degree deviate from
those presented, this will not affect in any way the outcome of this EIA.
In general the types of the bottom materials, of significance for the fairway dredging, and limited
to the shallow top layer of some 3-4 m thickness can be described as glacial till or "boulder clay"
under a blanket of fine to medium sand.
The upper sand layer, which was identified by available survey techniques, has a high degree of
dredgeabiiity. A reservation must be made for the possible occurrence of stones, cobbles and
boulders originating from the underlying boulder clay.
The boulder clay is close to rock stage, extremely tough to excavate. It is further characterised
by the enclosure of stones, cobbles and boulders of greatly varying degree of incidence. The
clay itself is very hard to dredge and even powerful excavating equipment will have a relatively
low production rate. The stones, cobbles and boulders constitute a very significant complication.
With larger sizes, the presence of these rocks will obstruct the excavation in an increasing
manner. It is thereby technically not feasible to establish with any precision the incidence of the
various classes of rock with regard to size by geotechnicaVgeophysical means.
A point of serious concern is the presence of contaminated sediments in the LEI dredging area.
Although all the contaminated sediments are located outside the area marked as the Worldbank
dredging area, they are located within the Port Entrance Rehabilitation project area. All
sediments located in the Worldbank dredging area are clean or only slightly contaminated. The
levels of contamination found in this area are so low that no restrictions are required in relation
to dredging, disposal and/or beneficial usage of these sediments. Details on sediment quality in
the Worldbank dredging area, the LEI dredging area and the non dredged part up to the Dane
River are presented in section 4.4.3 of this EIA.
For planning of the dredging works the entire dredging area has been divided by the LEI into 9
sub-areas (Figure 3-3). Unfortunately in the data presented by the LEI, the sediments in selected
areas are all categorised according the most difficult layer to be dredged. This means that in
areas where both fine sand and boulder clay is to be dredged, the information only displays the
total volume and the indication that it is boulder clay. In reality it might be considered to dredge
these two different sediment types separately, especially if contaminated sediments are to be
removed. This aspect should be realised while evaluating the sediment volumes given in Table
3-1. According the calculations of the LEI the total volume of "boulder clay amounts to 1,477,000
mi3, whereas the total volume of sand amounts to 412,000 m3.

DREDGING EQUIPMENT TO BE USED
Due to differences in the sediment characteristics (sand, silty sand and boulder clay), the levels

For the area between lines 71 - 27 (World Bank study area), a sensible dredging scenario could
be:
*  Remove the sand blanket above the glacial till as much as possible by Trailing Suction
Hopper Dredging and minimise the workload for stationary equipment.
* Apply stationary equipment, of which excavators mounted on a self-elevating platform with

For the area between lines 27 and 10 (LEI study area) the usage of a bucket dredger in
combination with a grab dredge is foreseen.
DISPOSAL OF DREDGED MATERIALS
According the LEI study the vast majority of the dredged sediments, including all the boulder clay
and the contaminated sediments will be disposed off at the marine dumpsite No 3, which is
located some 20-24 kilometres offshore. It is proposed to beneficially use the sands dredged
from the outer sea channel (between section 47 and 71), by placing these sediments north of the
North breakwater at a depth of 4 m.
In Section 7 of this EIA, recommendations on dredging and handling contaminated sediments,
as well as on additional options for beneficial use of the dredged sediments are presented.
3.2.2  Breakwater construction
In order to reduce wave heights within the port of Klaipeda, both breakwaters will be extended.
The North breakwater will be extended by about 250 m and the South breakwater will be
extended by about 350 m. The distance between the breakwater heads will be small enough to
reduce wave heights in the harbour adequately, but will be large enough to enable vessels
entering or departing safely (see Figure 3-1).
The breakwaters will be low crested, as the expected overtopping during wave attack is
acceptable for navigation. The breakwaters will not be accessible, so floating equipment will be
required to carry out maintenance.
The breakwater extensions will be of the rubble mound type, with a quarry run or gravel core. A
typical cross-section of the new breakwaters is presented in Figure 3-4. On the core a rock filter
layer will be placed to prevent the core material from being washed out. On the trunk sections,
on the filter layer a rock armour layer will be placed which can resist the wave attack and through
which the filter material can not be washed out. The heads of both breakwater extensions will be
armoured with concrete armour units. These units will be prefabricated at a construction site
near the breakwaters. At the toe of the breakwaters (the point where the armour layer reaches
the seabed), a toe protection will be constructed which gives support to the armour layer and
thus prevents the armour layer from sliding down. On both sides of the breakwaters a bottom
protection consisting of a rock layer on a geotextile membrane will be placed to prevent scouring.
The most probable construction method of the new breakwaters involves floating equipment.
The new breakwater heads will be located on the slope of the existing entrance channel. As the
breakwater heads will be constructed on a horizontal sea bottom, firstly a trench will be
excavated at the planned breakwater head location. Then the core of the breakwater will be
H7371   Draft Final Environmental Impact Assessment   3-7                      September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitaton Project                                         NA}
constructed by dumping quarry run or gravel using dump barges and profiling the material using
a pontoon mounted grab. The bottom and toe protection, under layers and armour layers will be
constructed using pontoons, floating cranes and tugs.
The construction of the extensions of the breakwaters involves about 270,000 m3 rock and
30,000 m3 concrete. The rock material for the breakwater works will be supplied from abroad,
either from Finland or Sweden. Aggregates and sand for the concrete armour units and possibly
gravel for the breakwater core will come from local borrow areas.
Figure 3-4    A typical cross-section of the new breakwaters
3.2.3  Wreck removal
Two shipwrecks are located near the head of the existing North breakwater. The wreck located
on the outside of the breakwater is the former Greek tanker "Globe Asimi", of which no data
could be retrieved regarding possible cargo remains. During the time of writing of this EIA, no
decision had yet been made with respect to the possible removal of this wreck.
The wreck located on the inside of the breakwater concerns the remains of the motor vessel
"Rudolf Breitcheid". This vessel, which is to be removed under the current project, ran aground
on a shoal near the head of the breakwater on 24 September 1988. At that moment the vessel
was carrying steel roles as cargo. During the accident the vessel broke in two. After the accident
the vessels cargo was unloaded, after which the vessel's bow part was taken to Finland.
Presently only the back part still remains.

4.1  GENERAL DESCRIPTION OF THE STUDY AREA
Klaipeda is located at a strait connecting the Kursiu

4.1.1  Baltic Sea Coastal area
To the south of Klaipeda a narrow peninsula separates
the Curonian lagoon from the Baltic Sea. This peninsula                       ng
is a sandy stretch of land extending 98 kilometres, with a
width varying from 400 meters to 3.8 kilometres. It was
formed some five to six thousand years ago, as sand
accumulated in the shallower waters along the Baltic  ;1
coast. Because of its unique scenic beauty and
ecological values the peninsula has been declared as a
national park: "the Kursiu Nerija National Park". The
area is one of the most popular and prestigious
recreation areas in Lithuania and its sand dunes, pine                      Tam
forests and 80 - 100 meters wide beaches attract tens
of thousands of holiday-makers every year. The national  "  :
park also includes a 2.5 kilometres wide sea zone along
the Curonian spit coast.
The first 6.5 kilometres of the Curonian spit (see Figure
4-2a) is called the Smiltyne area. This area belongs to
the Klaipeda municipality and has a total local population          *.l?
of 80 inhabitants. Most of the local inhabitants are
employed  in  the  Kursiu  Nerijos  National  Park
administration. The Smiltyne area is divided into five   Figure 4-1  Area map
functional subareas, being: an urbanised territory,
territories for intensive and extensive recreational use, a
landscape reserve and the water aquatory.
All land is state owned and its main function is recreational use. Industrial activities in this
area are prohibited. Of the total 47 buildings in this area 4 are living apartments and 70% of
the rest are recreational objects, which include: a maritime museum and aquarium, a
dolphinarium, a Curonian spit nature museum, 2 hotels and 6 pensions, a marina, the
administration office of the National park, a fisheries research laboratory, 5 cafes and 2 local
ferry terminals.
The coastal area to the north of Klaipeda consists of a 2 kilometre wide coastal zone from the
north breakwater to the Karkle settlement, which is located some 8 kilometres from the port
entrance. Two types of natural landscapes can be distinguished: sandy beaches and morenic
cliffs. The total surface area as indicated in Figure 4-2b is 982 ha.
H7371   Draft Final Environmental Impact Assessment   4-1                   September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                       H
HARRIS
Administratively this area belongs to the Klaipeda City's "green belt" (80%) and the
"Dutchman hat" landscape reserve (20%). About 70% of the area is covered by forests, 15%
are sand dunes and 15% is urbanised.
The bottom relief is characterised by landward elevation. In the northern part the elevation
reaches 10 m, while in the southern part it reaches 30 meters. The coastline is dominated by
sandy beaches, except for a small range near the "Dutchman hat", where gravel beaches can
be found. The forests growing on the sandy soils consist mainly of pine, birch and black alms.
These Northern Klaipeda suburbs and the Paiurio Landscape Park are important as
recreational zone for Klaipeda City. In the summer this area is attended by up to 2300 visitors
per day.
Small private houses dominate in the three settlements, The present populations of these
settlements are: Melnrage 1130 inhabitants, Melnrage II 41 inhabitants and Girulai 250
inhabitants. Child camps and pensions can be found in the Girulai area. The biggest industry
in this area is the Oil Exporting Plant situated in southern Melnrage. Most of the commercial
activities here are services and include: cafes, restaurants and pensions, a camping site,
children camps and other recreational services.

4.1.2   Klaipeda and its Port
The city of Klaipeda stretches along the Klaipeda Strait and is built according a linear plan.
The city has 202,000 inhabitants, making it the third largest city in Lithuania. The Port of
Klaipeda is the most northern ice-free port in the eastern part of the Baltic Sea.
Figure 4-3    Klaipeda Port areas
The Port is oriented in a South - North direction. The distance from the most northern point to
the most southern point is more than 1 1 km. The Port areas comprises more than 19 km of
quay walls, 8.3 km of which are used for cargo handling. The rest of the quay walls are used
for shipbuilding, ship repairing and other activities. At present the northern part of the port
has a depth in between -10.5 - -12.0 m. In other parts of the port depth varies between -8
and -1 2 m. The width of the Klaipeda strait varies from 0.4 - 1.1 km.
At present the port is able to accommodate ships of up to 200 m in length and with draughts
of 10.5m. Every year about 7000 ships enter the port from more than 50 foreign countries.
Via regular shipping lines Klaipeda Port is linked to various European and American
countries. There are well known lines to Kiel, Hamburg, Bremerhafen, Copenhagen,
Stockholm, Arhus and Gdynia and container lines to Rotterdam and Felixstowe. Hinterland
road and railway connections are good. The highway links Klaipeda to Kaunas, Vilnius, Minsk
and Moscow. Two railway stations serve the Port, whereas the nearest airport is in Palanga,
25 km away.
The most important types of the cargo in the Klaipeda port are: steal prodects - about 4.5
million tons, fertilisers - about 2 million tons, oil products - up to 5-6 million tons, wood
products - about 0.7 million tons, grain - about 0.5 million tons, reefer cargo - up to 1 million
tons, sugar - about 0.5 million tons and cement - up to 0.4 million tons.
In Klaipeda Port downtime in the port is linked to meteorological conditions. During strong
storms, in average occurring 20-25 days per year, ships can not enter or leave the port. In
some years this period can even be longer resulting in 45-50 downtime days in a year. Also
due to weather conditions the stevedoring companies cannot operate in between 15-25 days
per year.
The Klaipeda State Seaport Authority KSSA, which was founded in 1991, is in charge of the
functioning of the port and is responsible for maintenance, reconstruction and modernisation
of the Port infrastructure. Loading and unloading operations are being managed by separate
independent terminals. The land and the infrastructure of the Port belong to the state,
whereas the superstructure can be privatised. Besides some private stevedoring companies,
the Port includes several shipyards (both construction and repair), and the oil Terminal
"Klaipeda Nafta". In total more than 10000 employees work in the Klaipeda Port and related
H7371   Draft Final Environmental Impact Assessment   4-3                    September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                        m
HARRIS
industries. More information on specific aspects like vessel traffic control, and reception
facilities of the Port can be found in Section 4.7 of this report.
4.1.3   Curonian lagoon
The Curonian lagoon is a large shallow transitory freshwater body, situated in the
southeastern Baltic Sea and separated from the sea by the Curonian Spit. The surface area
of the lagopn is 1584 kM2, the longest axis is 93 km, the shortest axis is 46 km. The basin
contains about 6 km of water. The mean depth is 3.8 m, whereas the maximum depth of 5.8
m can be found in the southern region.
The southern and central portions of the lagoon are fresh water due to discharge from the
Nemunas River and other smaller rivers, maintaining a predominant flow from the south to
the north.
The northern part of the lagoon and the Klaipeda Strait are influenced by seawater intrusions
from the Baltic Sea. These rapid and irregular water exchanges cause large fluctuations in
temperature, salinity and other characteristics.
As the lagoon is relatively shallow, stratification of the water column, if present at all, is weak
and unstable. The large amount of nutrients transported by the rivers keep the lagoon in a
eutrophicated state.
Morphological properties of the lagoon and hydrodynamical unstability can be considered as
the key factors determining the main characteristics of water masses, bottom substrate,
distribution of pelagic and benthic communities and ecological problems as well.
In 1983 the Curonian spit was broken in its narrowest part near the town of Lesnoje (Russia),
due to a strong storm and an extreme Baltic Sea level rise. The seawater inflow through the
break did not cause permanent damage to the lagoon ecosystem.
4.2    CLIMATE
The climate of Lithuania is transitional between maritime and continental. In the 12-15
kilometres-wide coastal zone it is maritime, and in the eastern part of the country it is
continental. From the point of view of suitability for human health and economic activities the
climate can be considered to be among the favourable ones. It is characterised by seasonal
changes of temperature four times a year, by moderate heat in summer and by adequate
humidity and a sufficient number of bright days. The negative features include long autumns
and winters, and a relatively short vegetation period (169-202 days).
H7371   Draft Final Environmental Impact Assessment    4-4                    September 1999

4.2.2  Wind
Detailed wind information, based on data of 1947 - 1996 of Klaipeda Marine station, is
presented in the LEI report (Kaunas 1998) and can be summarised as follows:
Although wind is one of the most unstable meteorological elements and sudden changes of
weather are characteristic all year round, a distinct seasonal effect can be recognised in the
monthly mean values of the wind velocity and direction.
The prevailing wind direction is SE in the winter, westerly to northerly in spring, westerly in
summer and variable between W and SE in the autumn. The winds are weakest in spring and
highest in wintertime. Strong winds generally come from westerly to northerly directions (SW-
W-NW-N) and occur throughout the year. In some winters strong cold winds from the east
may persist for several weeks.
The all year long-term wind climate at Klaipeda is presented in Table 4-2. This table shows
the percentage of occurrence of winds of various strengths from each direction. From this
table it can be deducted that in about 80% of the time the winds are less than 10 m/s.

4.2.3   Fog and Ice formation
Both fogs and ice formation are meteorological conditions that cause trouble to the activities
in the port areas.
FOG
Fog can occur all year round, but two maximum occurrences can be observed: one in the
beginning of winter in December and one in spring in April. Fogs mostly occur when the wind
direction is from the west. A review of the average number of foggy days in Klaipeda is given
in Table 4-3.
Table 4-3
____________     ~Average_number of fo  dys~ in Klaipeda __

No of Days    3.4  4.0  5.9  6.0  5.7  3.6  2.4  1.9  2.7  3.4  3.5  4.4  47.0

in hours
ICE FORMATION
In wintertime the waters of the lagoon will freeze. The thickness of the ice in the lagoon at
Nida is approximately 65 - 70 cm in frosty winters. In the northern parts of the lagoon, up to
the Klaipeda Strait the ice is three times thinner and not thicker than 30 cm.
During mild winters or at the end of a frosty period, the ice cover at the lagoon may break up
due to termical cracks in the ice and high wind velocities resulting in the formation of drift ice.
These drifting ice formations may cause danger to navigation in the Klaipeda Strait. Very
intensive ice drifting period are also potentially dangerous for ships mooring near quay walls
and ships that cannot use the normal anchoring positions in the port. Intensive ice moving
H7371    Draft Final Environmental Impact Assessment    4-6                        September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                       I
HARRIS
periods, with ice from the lagoon floating to the sea through the Klaipeda Strait, usually last
for 3 to 10 days. Due to the influence of warmer water from the Baltic Sea, intensive
navigation, water depth and waves, the Klaipeda Strait does normally not freeze. Exceptions
were recorded for the winters of 1935 and 1936, when the Klaipeda strait was covered with
ice for a period of 20 - 30 days.
The Baltic Sea near Klaipeda (and consequently also the Klaipeda Strait) freezes only in very
cold and frosty winters. The last of these cold winters was in 1970, when all of the Baltic Sea
was covered by ice for more than one month. In milder winters small and large sized ice
patches may be found along the coast up to about 100 km offshore.
4.3    HYDRAULICS
4.3.1   Water levels and flows
The tidal motion in the Baltic Sea is very weak. Water level changes at sea are mainly
caused by wind set-up and at Klaipeda Port also by fresh water run-off. According to the
Admiralty Chart 2276, Chart Datum is approximately Mean Sea Level. Monthly mean water
levels presented in the LEI report (Kaunas 1998) show a seasonal variation with low values
(around -0.1 m) in springtime and high values (around +0.1 m) in the period from September
through January.
Data of extreme water levels at sea (station at Pionerskas) and in Klaipeda Strait (Klaipeda
Port) seem not fully consistent, possibly due to differences in the sampling periods, but do
indicate that a level of about +0.5 m is exceeded once per year and a level of +1.0 m is only
seldomly exceeded. The water level may drop below -0.5 m once every year and rarely below
-1.0 m. Extreme water levels always occur during extreme events and may fall back to MSL in
a period of one or two days in case of storms. In that period a large volume of water (approx.
200 million m3 per dm water level change) has to pass Klaipeda Strait to level the water level
in the lagoon with the sea. This may cause high flow velocities in Klaipeda Strait.
The statistical analysis of the water-level fluctuations at the Klaipeda water-level
measurement post (three kilometres inland from the harbour entrance) as carried out by the
Baltic Eco group over a period of 34 years (1950 to 1972 and 1978 to 1988) is presented in
Table 4-4.

When the flow is directed from the lagoon to the sea, the most recurrent water discharge in
the Klaipeda Strait is 1300 m3/s. During tides the discharge increases till 3250 m3/s, whereas
the average velocity of the flow increases to 0.8 m/s. The maximum conductivity of the Strait
is approximately 5000 m3/s, which corresponds to a flow velocity of 1.2 m/s.
Inflow into the lagoon from the sea on average occurs 40 times per year with a total duration
of 70 days. Wind set-up and density currents cause the inflow of salt sea water along the
bottom of Klaipeda Strait into the lagoon. In the period 1973-1981 the average annual inflow
amounted to 4.7 km3 and after deepening of the access channel it increased to 5.9 km3 in
the period 1982-1989. Usually the discharge during inflow from the sea is around 850 m3/s.
H7371   Draft Final Environmental Impact Assessment   4-8                   September 1999

HARRIS
However, during extreme storms it could reach as much as 3500 m3/s, with a corresponding
flow velocity of 1 m/s.
Sometimes intermediate conditions occur in the Strait. In those cases a fresh water surface
layer flows from the lagoon, whereas a salt bottom layer flows from the sea to the lagoon. The
discharges during these conditions, which occur in approximately 25% of the time are small,
and flow velocities may reach 0.2 m/s.

(1984-1989):

These flow conditions are supposed to be representative for the port up to the port entrance.

4.3.2  Waves
The Baltic Sea wave climate is mainly induced by wind. In general it can be stated that in the
Klaipeda water territory near the seashore, the biggest waves reach 3 to 5 meters. In the
open sea they reach 6 to 7 meters, whereas in exceptional situations they may reach more
than 9 meters.
OFFSHORE WAVE CLIMATE
For determination of the offshore wave climate near Klaipeda, model results from the wave
hindcast model of the British Meteorological Office have been used. The model returns wave
characteristics at specific gridpoints. Data, on which the model for the Baltic Sea is based,
are available for a 12-year period. The gridpoint for which the offshore wave climate is
determined is (55.8 ON, 20.7 E), where the present entrance to Klaipeda port is at (55.7 ON,
21.1 E).
For each directional sector of 30, the exceedance probabilities for different wave heights
have been determined with the model. Based on these probabilities, extreme significant wave
heights have been determined, see Table 4-7. In this table, only the wave heights for the
relevant directional sectors are presented. The table shows a dominant wave direction
between SW and W.

NEARSHORE WAVE CLIMATE
To obtain the nearshore wave climate, necessary as input characteristics in the breakwater
design, a mathematical wave model has been set up. The wave propagation modelling has
been carried out using the nearshore "Spectral Wind Waves module" of the two-dimensional
modelling package MIKE21, developed by the Danish Hydraulic Institute.
The wave propagation has been calculated for waves approaching from the sectors 180-0 ON
via west. In order to calculate the wave propagation from each direction correctly, three
models have been set up. The Southwest model is used for calculation of waves coming from
1800 and 210 N waves, the West model is used for 2400, 2700 and 300 ON waves and the
Northwest model for 3300 and 0 N waves. For more specific information on the models used
reference is made to the conceptual design report (Harris, 1998). The resulting significant
wave height and mean wave direction at the locations of the new North and South breakwater
are presented in Table 4-8.
Also, waves are registered in the coast hydrometeorological stations of Klaipeda (since
1948), Sventoji (1948 - 1958) and Nida (since 1954). Statistical analysis of available data
