6.5  IMPACT OF DREDGING ON THE STABILITY OF THE EXISITING
BREAKWATERS
When dredging to - 14 m is carried out near the existing breakwaters, the stability of these
breakwaters becomes at risk. The experts of Lenmorniiproekt as part of the LEI dredging study
studied this potential safety problem.
Based on the results of the stability calculations it was concluded that the stability of the southern
breakwater (and the coast of the Curonian Spit) is not at risk if the inclination of the slope is 1:7.
For the northern breakwater an inclination of the slope of 1:2.5 is sufficient to safeguard the
stability of the breakwater. By incorporating these stability aspects in the dredging design, this
potential dangerous impact has been eliminated._
H7371   Draft Final Environmental Impact Assessment    6-11                      September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                        HAIS
6.6  IMPACT ON NAVIGATION AND PORT OPERATIONS
It will be clear that during the construction activities, port operations and navigation should be
affected as little as possible. Due to the presence of dredging equipment, barges, pontoons,
anchor wires, construction areas, dredging and dumping operations, etc., some hindrance to
navigation and consequently port operations is unavoidable. During both the construction of the
breakwaters and the dredging operations, specific areas will be closed to navigation. By using a
trailing suction hopper dredger (TSHD) to remove the top sand layer hindrance to navigation is
strongly reduced, as the TSHD is not a stationary dredger. The backhoe hydraulic excavator on
a self-elevating platform as foreseen for dredging the boulder clay at the entrance channel, is not
dependent on an anchored wire system for mooring, so hindrance to navigation is reduced as
well. The bucket dredger on the other hand is expected to use a wired anchor system and will
consequently cause some hindrance to navigation. Carrying out the dredging works in smaller
strips, leaving ample space for ships to pass solves a part of this problem.
6.7   IMPACT OF CONSTRUCTION ACTIVITIES ON URBAN LAND TRAFFIC
The construction of the breakwaters involves some 270,000 m3 of rock and some 30,000 m3 of
concrete. It is not yet clear where the construction materials will come from and how they will be
transported to the construction site. If road transport is required for all or part of the construction
materials, e.g. trucks, a significant effect on road transport would be the result, including a
negative effect on air quality due to the emissions from exhausts of the vehicles. With rail or
maritime transport this effect would be negligible.
The same can be said about road transport by trucks of sand from a stockpile area to a beach or
dune area for replenishment, as this would involve large quantities of sand and consequently a
considerable number of trucks. These effects, although not crucial for the project, should be
reviewed carefully.
6.8  IMPACT ON RECREATION
Recreation on the beautiful sandy beaches north and south of the port entrance can be affected
in a number of ways. The worst that can happen is that a thin blanket of silt is deposited on the
beach. This effect can occur as a consequence of the dredging works in the Klaipeda Strait. It is
not guaranteed that this will occur, but if it does it will be local and of limited duration. In case the
environmental conditions along the coast would favour the presence of silt on the sandy
beaches, the large inflow of suspended sediments from the Curonian lagoon to the Baltic Sea
would have resulted in a thick layer of silt on the beaches already.
The dredged sands will be used for beach replenishment. Depending on the placing
methodology (on the beach or near shore) this will have a smaller or larger effect on recreation in
this area. The effect can be considered both negative and positive. Some people will find the
dredging works and pipelines annoying, whereas others see it as a tourist attraction in itself. It is
well known that beach replenishment projects in areas that are open to the public always attract
a lot of spectators. Consequently this effect is considered to be neutral.
However, special care should be taken in case of so-called mixed cargoes, i.e. when clay-balls or
silty sediments are present in the dredged sandy sediments. In view of the recreational value of
the beach areas, these cargoes should not be used for beach or dune replenishment. However,
when the cargoes contains limited amounts of clay-balls or silty sediments, they can be used for
H7371   Draft Final Environmental Impact Assessment   6-12                     September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                        9
HARRIS
foreshore replenishment. In case too much silt is present in the cargo, the load should not be
used for replenishment purposes, and should be redirected to the offshore disposal site.
6.9  POLLUTION DURING CONSTRUCTION
Pollution related to the construction activities can be caused by the equipment used, e.g.
dredgers, cranes, etc., and at the construction site(s), e.g. construction of concrete armour units,
storage and waste areas, etc.
POSSIBILITY OF OIL SPILLS FROM DREDGERS
The dredgers will probably bunker at the site. During bunkering activities oil spillage is the main
incident through which the aquatic environment may be affected. Fuel spillage might occur
principally by overflow and secondly during coupling and uncoupling of the hose. Accidental
spillage of oil or fuel can occur due to operations carried out with insufficient care, leaks (in e.g.
storage tanks, pipes, hoses) or accidents.
In order to minimise spillage the following measures have to be taken into account:
v Bunkering operations will only take place under safe weather and river conditions.
* The dredging operation will be stopped.
i The fuel tank will be sounded regularly during the bunkering operation to avoid spillage.
* All hoses will be sufficiently drained before being stowed.
OTHER SOURCES OF AQUATIC POLLUTION
Sanitary liquid waste originates from toilets, sinks, showers, laundry and galley. Although this
type of waste is oxygen consuming, it will be discharged in the surface waters, as the volumes
involved are small.
Industrial liquid waste is water containing oily substances originating from e.g. engine room,
pump room and decks (bilge water). In this respect it is to be checked if the dredgers (especially
the TSHD and the bucket dredger) are provided with a separator in compliance to the Marpol
Convention. In this way the bilge water is separated into sludge oil and purified water. The water
is pumped overboard and the sludge oil will remain on board in a sludge oil tank and will be
disposed of later in the port.
Pumproom water is not separated, due to the relatively large quantities that result when opening
the pumps. The water is directly pumped overboard.
Chemicals on board of the vessels might cause a potential risk for water pollution. It concerns
mainly the following items: fuel, lubricant oil, hydraulic oil, grease, chemicals (water treatment,
anti-freeze, degreasing products), paint, sludge (cleaning water containing oily substances).
Although usually the quantities of these chemicals are low, they should be properly stored in the
engine room, engine room store or paint store-roo.m.
The hydraulic installations on deck form a potential source of water pollution as rainwater might
drain hydraulic oil, spilled on deck due to possible leakages, over board. Spillage of oil from the
hydraulic installation should be kept at a minimum by adequate maintenance of the hydraulic
installation and timely replacements of worn parts.
H7371   Draft Final Environmental Impact Assessment   6-13                     September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                                      a
HARRIS
Solid waste like household waste, engine room wastes (e.g. cotton filters, grease, etc.) and deck
waste should be stored in garbage containers and disposed of in the port.
CONSTRUCTION AND WORKING SITES
After completion of the construction activities, the Contractor should ciear the working and
construction sites. All forms of waste should be removed, whereas places with soil pollution (if
any) should be treated.
H7371    Draft Final Environmental Impact Assessment    6-14                              September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                      9
HARRIS
7   ANALYSES OF ALTERNATIVES
7.1  OPTIONS FOR BENEFICIAL USE OF DREDGED SEDIMENTS
The main purpose of the dredging works at Klaipeda Port is to give larger vessels improved and
safe access to the port. Dredging is considered vital to the commercial activities, but clearly also
with respect to navigational safety of the Port. Perhaps the greatest problem concerning the
dredging operations is what to do with the material that is dredged.
Till today, all dredged sediments from both capital and maintenance dredging works in the study
area have been dumped at disposal sites in the Baltic Sea. The dredged sediments were always
looked at as a waste product, without any value. As a matter of fact it even costs money to get
rid of it, as the sediments have to be transported by barges over considerable distances to the
disposal site (>20 km).
Studies world-wide have shown that most dredged material is clean and suitable for beneficial
uses as restoring beaches, shore protection, topsoil for agricultural use, environmental
enhancement, construction material, and many other purposes. It has been realised that
dredged material can be a valuable resource and should not be easily considered for disposal.
The proposed capital dredging works, i.e. the deepening and widening of the entrance channel
and the northern part of the port, include excavation of approximately 200,000 m3 of clean sand,
more than 1,000,000 m3 of clean boulder clay and between 50,000 - 100,000 m3 of partly
contaminated silty sand.
In addition, yearly maintenance dredging volumes, consisting mainly of marine sands, are
foreseen totalling 200,000 - 300,000 m
BENEFICIAL USE OF MARINE SANDS
As discussed in Section 5.3 some coastal erosion takes place at various places north of the port
entrance. It is believed that this effect is mainly caused by the fact that yearly large quantities of
sand (> 200,000 m3) are removed from the active coastal zone by maintenance dredging of the
entrance channel. Relo.cating these dredged sands within the active coastal zone instead of
dumping these materials 20 km offshore, is expected to solve the coastal erosion problem.
Consequently, beneficial use, i.e. preventing coastal erosion, of all dredged sands is highly
recommended. This is also indicated in the LEI study (Kaunas, 1998).
It is advised to place the clean sandy sediments from the entrance channel (from both the
present project and future maintenance dredging), as closely as possible near the beach, at a
distance of a few kilometres on both sides of the outlet. If considered necessary, all or a part of
these sands can also be applied directly in beach or dune restoration projects or stockpiled for
future use.
Note: It has been decided by the KSSA to include this beneficial usage option for the marine
sands as part of the project.
BENEFICIAL USE OF BOULDER CLAY
At present, all dredged boulder clay is planned to be dumped at the offshore disposal site.
Boulder clay is rock-like material characterised by enclosures of stones, cobbles and boulders.
Boulder clay is not contaminated, an excellent construction material and should be considered
for beneficial uses as well. Options for beneficial use include:
H7371   Draft Final Environmental Impact Assessment   7-1                    September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                        H
HARRIS
Beneficial use of the boulder clay as construction material in the cores of the new
breakwaters. The core material of many dikes in the Netherlands consists of clay materials.
By replacing the quarry run or gravel by boulder clay considerable cost savings might be
achieved. However, it can be questioned whether this option would be technically feasible in
the Klaipeda situation.
Beneficial use of the boulder clay as construction material for the dikes of a confined
disposal area for contaminated sediments. Although the Port Authorities are faced with a
contaminated sediment problem, they are also blessed by having a solution at hand, i.e.
boulder clay. Boulder clay is an excellent isolating material and perfectly suited for
environmentally safe storage of contaminated sediments. With the boulder clay layer so
close to the surface and additional boulder clay at hand, an environmentally sound depot on
land can easily be constructed. Simply select a suitable location for a depot and remove the
top layer of soil till the boulder clay is reached. Construct dikes of boulder clay along the
sides and the depot is ready to be filled with contaminated sediments. The isolating
properties of the construction are such that it would even be acceptable to construct it on the
Curonian Spit (provided the location is suitable from other points of view).
* Beneficial use of the boulder clay for the construction of sills up-stream, if considered useful
for combating salt intrusion into the lagoon.
* In addition both boulder clay as such and the boulders may deserve stocking, so that both
can be used at a later stage for different applications. Boulders may even be used to create
artificial reefs, which would be beneficial to marine life and fisheries.
Note: At the time of writing this EIA only the separation and stockpiling of the boulders has been
considered. Evaluation of the other beneficial use options would require additional feasibility
studies for which no money was available.
7.2  OPTIONS FOR CONTAMINATED SEDIMENTS
The soil investigations as carried out by Geoprojektas have shown that practically all surface
sediments present in the LEI dredging area are contaminated (class 3 level of contamination
according Lithuanian classification system). According Lithuanian regulations these sediments
can only be dumped at sea in exceptional cases. Despite the contamination,'it is planned to
dispose these sediments in the Baltic Sea. This is considered to be in contrast with the
environmental protection policy of the Lithuanian Ministry of the Environment.
Under the Baltic Sea Joint Comprehensive Environmental Action Programme, Klaipeda was
identified as one of the pollution "hot spots" in Lithuania. Measures to improve the water quality
in and around Klaipeda are therefore listed as priority actions under the Baltic Sea Programme
approved by the regional Ministers of Environment at Helsinki (April 1992) and Gdansk (March
1993).
It is noted that the present project area is not the only location in Klaipeda Port where
contaminated sediments have been identified. Heavily contaminated sediments are also found in
Malku Bay (also considered for open sea disposal), Klasco commercial port, the Klaipeda Ship
Repair Yard, the bays of the ferry link, the-paper mill enterprise, the rail ferries swinging place,
Smelte Port and the Dane River mouth.
In 1995 a study was carried out in relation to "Dredging and disposal of contaminated sediments
in Klaipeda Port" by Haskoning (Nijmegen, 1995). This study resulted in the preliminary design
of two disposal areas for contaminated sediments. However, this project did not lead to the
H7371   Draft Final Environmental Impact Assessment    7-2                     September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Prolect                                          m
HARRIS
actual construction of a confined disposal area and hence no such disposal site for
contaminated sediments exists.
The construction of a disposal site for contaminated sediments is still part of the "Programme of
Construction and Reconstruction of Infrastructure objects of Klaipeda State Seaport up to the
year 2000". And secondly, the present Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project offers a unique
opportunity to solve the problem (see Section 7.1, beneficial use of boulder clay).
With more dredging works planned in the near future, the implementation of a confined disposal
facility (CDF) to store the contaminated sediment of the Klaipeda Port should be considered a
high priority item.
To solve the present and future contaminated sediment problems of the Port the
following action plan is recommended:
1: Quality and quantitv assessment of the contaminated sediments in the entire Port area
To determine the required capacity for a CDF additional field investigations based on core
drilling are required. The existing investigations are practically all limited to the top 5 centimetres
of the bottom sediments. Consequently it is not possible to make more or less accurate quantity
calculations. Rough estimates made in 1995 (Haskoning study) indicated the presence of
approximately 365.000 m3 of class 3 and 4 contaminated sediments in the entire Port area. In
addition an unknown volume of contaminated sediments will be newly formed in the years
ahead. In 1999, Lithuanian experts estimated that approximately 200.000 m3 of contaminated
sediments are still present in the Klaipeda port. The balance is made by the ongoing dredging
activities in Klaipeda Port and disposal of these sediments at sea.
With most of the investigations based on a limited number of contaminants, it is recommended
to include toxicity testing (bioassay investigations) as a prime method to assess the risk levels of
the contamination present. Subsequently, dredging activities should not be allowed in areas
proven to contain toxic levels of contamination, until a sound solution for handling the toxic
sediments has been arranged.
2: Investigate treatment ontions
In view of the limited volume of the contaminated sediments and the relatively high sand
contents, it is worthwhile to investigate if treatment of all or a part of the contaminated sediments
is feasible. This treatment may range from simple fraction separation to separate the (clean)
sand from the (contaminated) silt fraction, to complete destruction or removal of the
contaminant(s). Fraction separation is a relatively cheap and commonly used technique
nowadays, whereas special cleaning techniques are more costly. These costs should be
compared to the costs of constructing a small disposal facility.
In case a confined disposal site for the contaminated sediments appears to be the best solution,
the boulder clay originating from the deepening dredging works of the Port Entrance
Rehabilitation project should be considered as a construction material.
3: Dredge separately and in line with accepted methodologies
The contaminated sediments should be removed separately and according environmentally
sound and accepted dredging methodologies. These types of dredging works are not the same
as normal maintenance dredging works.
Based on studies and contaminated sediment site remediation projects carried out during the
past seven years by the author (van Oostrum, 1992 - 1998) the following key elements in
dredging contaminated sediments are identified:
H7371   Draft Final Environmental Impact Assessment   7-3                      September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                           m
HARRIS
*  High accuracy dredging, resulting in complete removal of only the contaminated sediments.
This is both an environmental and an economic element. It requires high accuracy site
investigations and high accuracy dredging monitoring systems.
*  Minimising spreading of contaminants. This is an environmental element and requires
measures to prevent or reduce turbidity and/or systems to isolate the resuspended
sediments (silt screens).
*  Minimising the quantity of process water. This is an economic element and of interest in view
of storage capacity or cost of transport and/or disposal.
*  Personnelprotection. This element is a human element.
7.3  EVALUATION OF ALTERNATIVES
The following alternatives have been considered for evaluation of the effects:
Alternative 1: No-action, the so-called zero alternative
In this alternative the present situation will remain unchanged. The proposed project will not be
executed, which means no dredging and construction activities will be carried out. This
alternative is taken as the "neutral" reference for comparison of the other two alternatives.
Alternative 2: The proposed project
This alternative includes the construction of two new breakwaters and dredging of approximately
2 million m3 of sand, silt and glacial till sediments. In the proposed project, all dredged sands
(from the outer entrance channel) will be beneficially used for nearshore or beach replenishment.
All silty sediments as well as all the glacial till sediments will be disposed off at the designated
offshore disposal site. In this alternative all non sand sediments will dredged as one volume,
which means that no differentiation will be made between clean and contaminated sediments
and between silty sand and glacial till.
Alternative 3: More environmentally friendly alternative
This alternative is the same as the proposed project, but with some changes in the execution of
the dredging works. In this alternative the contaminated sediments present in the LEI dredging
area, will be dredged separately from the clean sediments and subsequently stored in a confined
disposal area. Dredging of the contaminated sediments will be done in line with modern practice
of removing contaminated sediments, i.e. with high dredging accuracy, minimal turbidity and
resuspension of contaminated sediments and minimal spill.
In addition boulders from the glacial till will be collected for beneficial use elsewhere, while
options for beneficial use of the glacial till will be studied in more detail.
7.3.1   Review of evaluation results
(see Table 7-1)
EFFECTS DURING OPERATIONS
The following effects are related to the newly created situation and consequently have a more or
less lasting nature.
*    Hydraulics                       _  _
Due to the construction of the new breakwaters and the reduced opening width of the port
entrance, locally some slightly higher current velocities are to be expected. Due to deepening
and widening of the entrance channel and the northern port area, the hydraulic resistance of the
Klaipeda Strait will be permanently reduced. As a result, water discharge rates in both directions
may increase by 3 - 4%.
H7371   Draft Final Environmental Impact Assessment    7-4                       September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                        H
HARRIS
The related slightly higher currents may locally lead to slightly increased bottom erosion and
reduced rates of sedimentation of suspended matter in the Klaipeda Strait. However these
effects are expected to be rather small and are neither very favourable nor very unfavourable.
* Wave climate inside Port
Computer modelling showed that the construction of the new port layout will result in
considerable reduced wave penetration. Short wave heights will be reduced by 5 - 15 %,
whereas long wave heights will be reduced by approximately 25%. These permanently reduced
wave heights will have a very beneficial effect on shipping and navigational safety.
*   Navigational conditions and safety
Due to better wave protection, additional stopping length, increased manoeuvring space and the
new alignment of the inner channel, the navigational conditions will be greatly improved by the
project. Besides, as a consequence of the better wave protection the tugs can be fully effective
and operational under all required conditions, including emergency conditions. The improved
navigational conditions and tug effectiveness also directly lead to more safe nautical conditions.
* Environmental risks
The environmental risks are mainly related to the risks of oil spills, which can be caused by
collisions between ships (bad manoeuvrability) or when a non-tug-assisted tanker or other ship
hits one of the breakwaters. The improved navigational conditions of the fairway, the improved
working conditions for tugs to provide assistance and the realignment of the inner channel away
from the oil terminal berths, greatly reduce accident risks. This can be considered a major and
permanent positive effect of the project.
- Coastline erosion / development
Although a difference of opinion exists between scientists about the littoral drift in the study area,
the most likely theory is that the nett littoral drift is negligible or at least small. Consequently, the
presence of the new breakwaters as such will not have a major effect on coastline development.
All parties agree that the removal by maintenance dredging of large quantities of sand from the
coastal zone system is one of the most important factors affecting the coastline. As in the
proposed project all sand dredged from the entrance channel will be relocated within the coastal
zone system (nearshore directly north and south of the breakwaters), the project is not expected
to have a significant effect on coastline development.
* Maintenance dredging
In spite of the extensions of the breakwaters, the deepening and widening of the access channel
will distinctly increase the annual maintenance dredging volumes and thus the annual
maintenance. dredging costs. As indicated above the removal of large quantities of sand from
the coastal system will in time lead to coastal erosion problems. If relocation of sands from the
entrance channel to the nearshore areas will also be practised with all future maintenance
dredging works in stead of offshore disposal, it is anticipated that the present coastal erosion will
be stopped or at least significantly reduced. In that case the negative effect on maintenance
dredging will be limited to increased dredging costs.
* Salt intrusion in the lagoon
In all alternatives, including the present situation, salt water will flow to the lagoon during periods
of wind set-up from the Baltic Sea. Due to the reduced hydraulic resistance in the Klaipeda Strait
the exchange of water between the lagoon and the Baltic Sea will be slightly facilitated.
Consequently the volumes of water exchange (in both directions) may increase between 0 and
4%, depending on weather and waterlevel conditions at a specific time. The affected areas in
the lagoon are relatively small when compared to the total surface area of the lagoon and the
scale of the effect on salt water intrusion is well within the natural variability.
H7371   Draft Final Environmental Impact Assessment   7-5                      September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                           9
HARRIS
Fisheries
The changes in available fishing areas in the two alternatives, which include dredging and the
construction of breakwaters, are negligible. Also the fact that the outflow of fresh water will be
further into the Baltic Sea is not expected to have a significant effect on fisheries. More
important is the increase in hard substrate surface area for spawning and shelter as a direct
consequence of the construction of the new breakwaters. The importance of the existing
breakwaters is this respect is demonstrated by recent studies.
*   Aquatic life
The effects on aquatic life in the Baltic Sea are mainly related to the redirection of the outflow of
fresh water from the lagoon to a position further in to the sea and the creation of new hard
substrates for benthic life. Both aspects will have a beneficial effect on aquatic life in the area.
The effects on aquatic life in the Curonian lagoon are mainly related to the slight increase of salt-
water inflow into the lagoon. As this effect will be well within natural variability no changes in
species composition are to be expected. Due to the increased inflow of salt water, both the salt
water zone and the frontal zone (between salt and fresh water), which is relatively rich in
species, may slightly widen. As a result the densities of species of marine origin may slightly
increase.
* Water quality at disposal site
Since 1987, large volumes of sand, silt and boulder clay originating from dredging works have
been placed at the selected offshore disposal site. The disposal of approximately 1.5 million m3
of uncontaminated dredged sediments from the proposed project over a period of several years
in not expected to have a significant and lasting effect on water quality in the area. However in
case also contaminated sediments are dumped at this site, the contaminated sediments will act
as a long-lasting source of pollution. Consequently water quality will be negatively affected for
many years.
EFFECTS DURING CONSTRUCTION
The following effects are related to the dredging and construction activities and consequently are
of a temporary nature. They will stop after the project activities have been completed.
* Water quality
Resuspension of sediments and the release of contaminants will negatively affect water quality
during dredging and disposal works, but also during the construction of the breakwaters (placing
of construction materials). In case the contaminated sediments are removed separately from the
clean sediments and according an adapted dredging methodology (practically zero turbidity), the
resuspension of contaminated sediments and consequently the negative effects on water quality
can be strongly reduced. At the offshore disposal site the impact of the dumping operations on
the suspended solids regime is negligible. However, disposal of contaminated sediments will
locally negatively effect water quality.
*  Aquatic life
These effects are restricted to the actual dredging and construction site, and include the removal
of benthic organisms during dredging, increased turbidity levels and reduced visibility and
possible smothering of benthic organisms and roe. Based on the characteristics of the highly
dynamic coastal zone the removal of benthic animals can be considered of little importance. The
resuspension of sediments and subsequFent -resettling will be of importance for both fish
migration and fish spawning. In case contaminated sediments are resuspended, the effects will
be more severe. At the offshore disposal site, blanketing of the seabed is the most significant
physical effect. As more than 10 million m3 of dredged sediments have already been dumped
here in the last 10 years, the effects on benthic life are limited in case clean sediments are
H7371    Draft Final Environmental Impact Assessment    7-6                       September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                          HARRIS
dumped. Disposal of contaminated sediments will have a much more profound negative effect
on aquatic life.
*  Fisheries
Dredging and especially its effect on water quality may have a significant effect on migrating fish
species and fish spawning. Mitigating measures (section 8) are foreseen to minimise these
effects. The effects on fisheries at the offshore disposal site are limited, as this area has already
been in use as a disposal site for dredged materials for riore than 10 years. However care
should be taken that disposal of dredged sediments is restricted to the designated disposal site.
* Navigation and Port operations
No doubt the dredging and construction activities will cause some hindrance to navigation and
consequently to port operations, as parts of the port area and the navigational channel will be
temporarily closed for navigation. The areas will be limited to the construction areas of the
breakwaters and the areas where boulder clay is to be removed by stationary dredging
equipment.
* Urban land traffic
The effects on urban land traffic are related to transport of construction materials for the
breakwaters to the construction site and road transport of dredged sand by trucks from a
stockpile area to neighbouring beach or dune areas. Depending on the scale of these activities
both may have a significant effect on existing traffic flows.
*   Recreation
The effects on recreation are related to the presence of dredging related equipment on the
beaches (in case of beach replenishment), increased turbidity levels in the coastal waters and
the construction of the breakwaters. These effects are rather difficult to evaluate, as they can be
considered either positive, neutral or detrimental depending on the viewpoint taken. Breakwater
and dredging construction sites often attract many spectators and can even become tourist
attraction sites. However, other people may favour the scenery of wide-open water and
undisturbed endless beaches. Care should be taken during the replenishment works that only
sand mixtures are deposited on the beaches. Mixed cargoes with clay-balls and / or mud should
only be used for nearshore replenishment, or should be redirected to the offshore disposal site.
This is to be part of the monitoring program.
SUMMARY EVALUATION (see Table 7-1)
Major positive effects are expected in relation to navigational conditions and safety, and the
related reduction of oil spill risks. The new breakwaters will also have a small positive effect on
fisheries and aquatic life in the project area.
The project is expected to result in higher future maintenance costs and will have a negative
effect on water quality in the Baltic Sea if contaminated sediments are dumped at the offshore
disposal site.
During construction several detrimental effects are to be expected. However, as all of these
effects are related to the construction and dredging activities, they are all of a temporary nature.
This means the effects will stop once the project is finished. Included in these temporary effects
are detrimental effects on water quality and aquatic life, especially if contaminated sediments are
dredged and dumped without precautions. Smalrdetrimental effects are expected in relation to
fisheries, navigation (hindrance) and urban land traffic (hindrance).
Mitigating measures to minimise the indicated negative effects will be presented in section 8 of
this report.

7.3.2  Preferred alternative
Alternative 3 has been selected as the so-called Preferred Alternative and was presented
accordingly to the Port Authorities in the draft EIA (September 1998). This alternative was found
to have the same benefits as alternative 2, but the least and less severe negative impacts, while
still meeting the goal of the Client, e.g. a safer and more economic port.
7.4  ENCROACHEMENT  ON  PROPOSED  ACTION  AND  PREFERRED
ALTERNATIVE
During the execution of the EIA study for the proposed project, upon KSSA's initiative the area
to be dredged under this project was split into two tenders. One tender organised by Frederic R.
Harris (FRH) and financed by a World Bank load, covering the (re)construction of the
breakwaters and the dredging (practically) from the existing coastline seawards. The other
tender organised by the Lithuanian Energy Institute (LEI) and financed by KSSA itself, covering
the dredging from the existing coastline land inwards. The dredging area under the FRH tender
H7371   Draft Final Environmental Impact Assessment   7-8                      September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                         AI
HARRIS
comprises only clean sediments, whereas practically all surface sediments under the LEI tender
can be classified as contaminated under the Lithuanian classification system.
In view of the fact that a CDF had not yet been implemented, the KSSA requested permission
from the Lithuanian Ministry of the Environment to be allowed to dump the contaminated
sediments present in the dredging area covered under the LEI tender at sea. Although not in line
with the concept of environmental protection, or the international attempts to improve the water
quality of the Baltic Sea - measures to improve the water qual.6y In and around Klalpeda are
listed as priority actions under the Baltic Sea Programme approved by the regional Ministers of
Environment at Helsinki (April 1992) and Gdansk (March 1993) - this permission was granted
and early 1999 dredging in the LEI area started. During the summer of 1999 practically all
contaminated and clean sediments had been dredged in the LEI dredging area and had been
dumped offshore.
Consequently, with no contaminated sediments present in the dredging area covered under the
FRH tender and all the contaminated sediments already removed from the LEI dredging area,
the so-called preferred alternative as developed in this EIA appears no longer relevant for this
project.
However, there is still a considerable volume of contaminated sediments left in various parts of
the Klaipeda port. Lithuanian experts estimate the present volume of class 3 and 4 sediments at
approximately 200.000 m3. Undoubtedly, more contaminated sediments will be formed
(deposited) in enclosed port areas in the years ahead. This clearly demonstrates that the
implementation of a CDF is still very relevant.
According the Minister of Transport and Communications, Mr. R. Didziokas, the project for
storage of contaminated sediments will form part of the Public Investment programme and the
Tina programme as a separate project. The implementation of this project is anticipated in 2001.

8  ENVIRONMENTAL MANAGEMENT PROGRAM
8.1  BACKGROUND
Based on the findings of the EIA it is clear that the execution of the Klaipeda Port Entrance
Rehabilitation Project as funded by the Worldbank, will influence a variety of environmental
aspects. Therefore an Environmental Management Program (EMP) has been developed, which
contains the evaluation of the most significant environmental effects, defines adequate
measures to mitigate them, and establishes a monitoring program to measure and control both
the impacts and the effectiveness of the mitigating measures.
The general objectives of the EMP are:
1. to ensure compliance with all pertinent environmental legislation
2. to ensure environmental-friendly practices in relation to dredging and disposal works
3. to give priority to preventive measures in preference to corrective measures
4. to promote two-way communication with the local communities
The works, activities and areas considered under this EMP are limited to the works as financed
by the Worldbank and include:
* All dredging, disposal and reclamation works, including deepening and widening of the
entrance channel, beach/foreshore replenishment, and stockpiling of dredged materials or
parts thereof.
. All breakwater construction and repair works, including transport and stockpiling of
construction materials.
* All survey, soil investigations, testing and monitoring works.
* All worksites and offices.
NOTE: Several aspects of the works are still unclear, e.g. the equipment and working
methods of the selected contractor, the source and transport of the breakwater
construction materials, etc. Consequently, the EMP in this section is to be considered a
DRAFT version, which is to be elaborated when the selected contractor has made
relevant details available.
In section 8.5 additional works directly related to this project are identified. These works
comprise:
* The setup of a nautical and environmental database system for storage and retrieval of
relevant data and information for better planning of future development projects, including
dredging and disposal works.
* Port wide site investigations to accurately assess the layer thickness and volumes of the
contaminated sediments, as well as its toxicity and dredgeability (need depending on scope
of ongoing studies).
* The development of a CDF for storage of contaminated sediments.
8.2  ANTICIPATED ADVERSE EFFECTS AND PROPOSED MEASURES
On the basis of the information provided in the EIA (section 1 to 7), a matrix of the
environmental aspects has been prepared, which summarizes possible relevant effects on the
natural and social environment. This matrix has been used to facilitate the definition of the
mitigating measures and the development of the monitoring program.
The mitigating measures as well as the monitoring activities are discussed in more detail in
section 8.3 and 8.4 respectively. For easy reading reference numbers are provided in the matrix.
H7371   Draft Environmental Impact Assessment  8-1                          September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                        HARRIS
8.3    MITIGATING MEASURES
Environmental Impact Assessment studies are designed to identify environmental problems,
which may be caused by a development project, and to determine the magnitude of the effects
on the environment. Through this process, design and operational changes can be introduced in
the detailed design phase of the project, thereby minimizing any adverse effects of the
development.
During the past five years the independent Environmental Impact Assessment Committee in the
Netherlands noted, that less and less mitigating measures were required after the EIA had been
completed. The pure fact that it is known to the project developers that an EIA will have to be
made, automatically resulted in more environmental friendly project proposals. Just like technical
and economical aspects are taken into consideration during the initial drafting of the project, so
are environmental aspects.
This is also true for the Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation project. The design of both the
entrance channel and the new breakwaters was oriented towards providing better protection
against waves and improvement of the navigational and safety conditions. This by itself strongly
reduces the risks of oil spills and is to be noted as a major benefit for the environment. With the
new layout (and other safety measures taken) the port entrance design will comply with
international safety standards.
The beneficial usage of dredged sand for beach or nearshore replenishment was also based on
environmental considerations, i.e. preventing further coastal erosion. This will be the first time
dredged sediments will be beneficially used in Lithuania.
Nevertheless, for some aspects of the project mitigating measures have been identified to
prevent or reduce possible detrimental effects. Two measures are related to the operational
phase (consequences) of the project, whereas the remaining measures are related to the
construction phase of the works.
8.3.1  MITIGATING MEASURES RELATED TO THE OPERATIONAL PHASE OF THE PROJECT
Set-up of an automated database system
Future maintenance dredging costs are expected to increase as more sedimentation in the
navigational channel is anticipated. In this respect it is important to note, that the removal of
sediments by dredging from the coastal zone with disposal offshore has been identified as one
of the possible causes of coastal erosion along the Klaipeda coastal area. To facilitate the
planning of beneficial usage of the sediments originating from maintenance dredging works (e.g.
relocating the sediments at appropriate locations within the coastal zone, beach replenishment,
etc.), a database system is to be set up. Information regarding the locations, types, quality and
quantities of the sediments to be dredged are stored in the database for future analyses. With
sediment characteristics and quantities known in advance (proven records), beneficial usage
can be better planned. This database system should be easy accessible and PC based. In
addition to storage of the sediment characteristics of maintenance projects, the database can
also be used to store other soiVsediment-related information and other environmental relevant
information. This would facilitate future planning-of development projects by the Port Authorities.
More detailed information regarding the development of an environmental and nautical database
system is presented in section 8.5.1.
H7371   Draft Environmental Impact Assessment  8-5                             September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                        HARRIS
Introduction of alien species
The increase in size and number of ships entering the port will result in increased risk of alien
species invasion. To mitigate this effect, which is associated with ballast water, appropriate
measures as indicated in the IMO guidelines should be taken by the Port Authorities.
8.3.2  MITIGATING MEASURES RELATED TO THE CONSTRUCTION PHASE OF THE PROJECT
During the construction ohase some temporary negative effects are foreseen. For these effects
the following mitigating measures are developed:
Protection of fish migration routes and spawning areas
The Lithuanian Ministry of the Environment has already to some degree regulated dredging
operations, which might interfere with fish migration. These regulations are known as "Order No
67" and are called "On the assessment of the effects of Klaipeda port dredging works on
fisheries" (included as appendix B to this report). These regulations comprise both strong and
very week points. Strong points are that dredging is only allowed during fish spawning migration
in case of "urgent necessity". Secondly, the dredging contractor is to provide information
regarding the planned dredging works and the measures taken to reduce the negative effects on
fish migration. In case of dredging during the fish spawning migration periods the dredging
contractor is to pay a fee for possible damage caused.
Very weak points are that the fees are so low that they will not put any restriction on dredging
from a financial point of view. Secondly, in the course of the dredging works the port must carry
out a monitoring investigation of migration intensity and the effects of dredging on migrating fish.
Assessment of the latter is believed to be practically impossible, as there are too many other
parameters besides dredging which might affect fish migration (natural variability of currents,
flow directions, discharge of waste water, spills, shipping, other port related activities, etc.).
Thirdly, the regulations do not in any way protect the spawning areas on the existing
breakwaters.
In view of the above, the dredging contractor should plan the dredging works outside the fish
spawning migration periods to the maximum extent possible. Besides, the Contractor is to take
protective measures for the breakwater spawning areas (to prevent smothering by resettling
sediments), if and when required.
As less intense fish migrations across the Klaipeda Strait take place throughout the year,
dredging and the resulting increased levels of resuspended sediments are likely to affect fish
migration in any period of the year. To mitigate these effects special attention should be paid to
predicting, monitoring and minimizing turbidity generation during the dredging operations.
Dredging clean and contaminated sediments
The lack of differentiation between dredging clean and contaminated sediments will result in
negative effects on water quality (resuspension and dispersion of contaminated sediments and
release of contaminants to the water column), aquatic life and fisheries. Besides, offshore open
water disposal of contaminated sediments will not only have a temporary and local negative
effect on water quality (during disposal), but also a more permanent and more widespread
negative effect. The contaminated sediments will be dispersed over a wide area (lithodinamically
active zone) and will act as a source of pollution.
The effects in the dredging areas can be mitigated by removing the contaminated sediments
separately from the clean sediments in a manner appropriate for the removal of contaminated
sediments (high accuracy dredging, no or minimal turbidity generation and minimal spillage).
The dredging contractor should prepare a method statement on the removal of the contaminated
sediments, in line with modern dredging practice.
H7371   Draft Environmental Impact Assessment  8-6                             September 1999



Jaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitabon Project                                         HARRIS
HARRIS~~~~~~~~
Disposal of contaminated sediments
The effects in the disposal area can be mitigated by not allowing contaminated sediments
(above a certain level of contamination) to be dumped at sea. A confined disposal area should
be prepared for safe storage of these sediments.
In addition, periodic testing should be carried out to verify that the sediments, which are to be
dumped at the offshore disposal site, do not contain hazardous materials.
Note: In December 1998 the Lithuanian Ministry of the Environment approved the request by
KSSA to dredge the LEI dredging area and to dump the contaminated sediments at sea. Early
1999 these dredging works started and by mid 1999 these works will have been completed.
Dredging was carried like normal maintenance dredging without any precaution to the
environment. Besides, the methodology used is not likely to result in complete removal of the
contaminated sediments. With practically all the contaminated sediments removed from the
study area and no contaminated sediments found present in the remaining Worldbank dredging
area, the above indicated mitigating measures for dredging and disposal of contaminated
sediments are considered no longer relevant for the dredging works forming part of the World
Bank project. However, as there is still a considerable volume of contaminated sediments left in
various parts of the Klaipeda port, the implementation of a CDF is still very relevant. More
detailed information regarding the development of a CDF is presented in section 8.5.3.
Offshore disposal of dredged sediments
At present four open water disposal areas for dredged sediments exist in the Klaipeda coastal
zone. Two of these sites have been closed, whereas the other two are still in operation. A fifth
disposal area is being studied. All these disposal sites will positively or negatively affect
fisheries. Disposal of glacial till sediments (including rocklike hard clay and boulders) is planned
to take place at disposal area 111, which is located more than 20 kilometers from the Port
entrance. The presence of mounds of rocklike clay and boulders make these areas less suitable/    Z
attractive for certain types of fishing (bottom trawling). To minimize the damage to fisheries
caused by disposal of dredged sediments, disposal should be restricted to the designated
disposal site. However, in view of the long transport distance to this disposal site and the related
costs, it is not unthinkable that disposal of dredged sediments from barges also takes place at
shorter distances from the port entrance. These "unplanned" and uncharted dumpings at various
locations between the port entrance and the official disposal site have already caused serious
damage to the fishing industry in general (see section 6.4) and fishing gear in particular.
To ensure proper disposal of the dredged sediments, the barges should be equipped with a GPS
(or better) positioning system and a PC-based electronic monitoring system for continuous
recording of the parameters time, position and load data.
Beach or foreshore replenishment
The sandy sediments dredged at the entrance channel will be beneficially used for prevention
and remediation of coastal erosion. However, special care should be taken in case the sandy
sediments contain inclusions of clay-balls or silty sediments. In view of the recreational value of
the beach areas, these so-called "mixed cargoes" should not be used for beach or dune
replenishment. When the cargoes contain limited amounts of clay-balls or silty sediments, they
can be used for foreshore replenishment. In case too much silt is present in the cargo, the load
should not be used for replenishment purposes, but should be redirected to the offshore disposal
site.
Planning of navigation during the construction works
To minimize the interference of stationary dredging equipment and the construction of the
breakwaters with other maritime traffic two mitigating measures should be taken. Firstly,
planning of the works should be done in such a way that the interference with other maritime
traffic is already minimized. The contractor should provide a method statement in this respect.
Secondly, a program should be developed by the Port Authorities in advance of the works, to co-
ordinate and further reduce this interference. This program is to include aspects like advance
H7371   Draft Environmental impact Assessment  8-7                             September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                          H
HARRIS
warning to other maritime traffic of closure of areas and presence of equipment, but also
advance warning to the contractor(s) of relevant maritime traffic, e.g. arrival or departure of oil
tankers or other large ships.
Hindrance and information to the public
No matter how well planned, the construction of the new breakwaters, the repair works for the
existing breakwaters and the dredging and replenishment works will cause hindrance to the
people who are living, working or recreating at or near these sites. To mitigate this effect, ample
attention should be paid to informing the public about the project, its timing and its progress.
Planning of road transport during the construction works
In case considerable road transport is foreseen as a consequence of the works (e.g. supply of
breakwater construction materials to the site and transport of sand to beach and/or dune areas),
more or less identical mitigating measures (see planning of navigation) should be taken with
respect to road transport.
Pollution caused by the construction activities
Pollution related to the construction activities can be caused by the equipment used, e.g.
dredgers, cranes, etc., and at the construction site(s), e.g. construction of concrete armor units,
storage areas for solid and liquid wastes, storage areas for stockpiling construction materials,
etc.
To mitigate these forms of pollution, the contractor should be requested to supply an anti-
pollution method statement. In this statement measures taken to prevent or minimize pollution,
including spillage during bunkering and waste handling, should be indicated. The statement
should also include a clean-up plan to be carried out after completion of the works.
NOTE: In the contractual arrangements relating to the environmental and social
management of the project, the above mitigating measures will be included. (Conditions
of Particular Application of the contract between the KSSA and the Contractor).

Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                        HIS
8.4  ENVIRONMENTAL MONITORING
The main objectives of the monitoring program can be described as:
*  The works should comply with laws, rules, regulations and permit requirements. This is the
legal basis for the monitoring program.
*  The learning objective for future planning. This is the common sense basis for the
monitoring program, and includes questions like:
- Are the project induced environmental changes in line with the expectations as
presented in the EIA and are additional mitigating measures required (e.g. coastline
development)
- How can we benefit from  the present project in view of the planned additional
development projects in the Klaipeda Strait?
- Which problems can we prevent in future works?
- How much money can we save in the future?
With respect to the proposed project and in line with the mitigating measures, the monitoring
activities can be split into two sections, i.e. monitoring related to the operational phase of the
new Port entrance (design consequences) and monitoring related to the construction activities of
the project (operational control).
The monitoring activities related to the operational phase are long term monitoring activities and
fall under the responsibility of the Port Authorities. The monitoring activities related to the
construction activities are mainly control monitoring activities and are the responsibility of the
Contractor and/or the Port Authorities. Management and execution of the monitoring activities
are discussed in section 8.4.3.                                                                  f
8.4.1  MONITORING RELATED TO THE OPERATIONAL PHASE OF THE PROJECT
Permanent reduction in hydraulic resistance in the Klaipeda Strait
Due to the dredging works in the sea access channel and the northern harbor area, the flow
conditions in the Klaipeda Strait will change. The expected permanent reduction of the hydraulic
resistance of the Strait will have a variety of secondary effects, like:
*  changes in flow characteristics and discharge rates
-  changes in sediment transport and sedimentation/erosion processes,
* changes in salt intrusion into the lagoon,
*  water level changes in the lagoon
Based on computer modeling, it is expected that the present project may result in a 3-4% initial
increase in discharge and may lead to approximately 2 cm lower water levels in the lagoon
during outflow periods.
Based on the LEI dredging study (LEI 1997), it is clear that considerable additional deepening
dredging works are foreseen for the area from the present project up to Alksnyne (more than 5
kilometers in the direction of the lagoon). If executed these dredging works will lead to a much
larger reduction in hydraulic resistance (up to 10%) and subsequently in much stronger
secondary effects. In order to be able to indicate the environmental effects of the planned future
works with more accuracy the effects of the present project should be assessed by monitoring
several key characteristics before and after the present project. The key characteristics should
include: waterflows in time, suspended sediment levels, salt intrusion measurements and water
level registrations.                    -
Several of these measurements are already included in ongoing monitoring programs, but
coordination may be required. Centralized storage of the resulting monitoring data in a PC-
based database system is highly recommended (see section 8.5.1).
H7371   Draft Environmental Impact Assessment  8-9                             September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                        HARRIS
Coastline development
A clear difference of opinion exists between scientists about the littoral drift in the study area.
Depending on the expert the execution of the project (and mainly the construction of the
breakwaters), may have a considerable or an insignificant effect on coastline development. To
make sure severe coastal erosion effects are noted in time to take preventive or mitigating
actions, the coastline both north and south of the access channel should be monitored.
The information should not only include details of the actual location of the coastline (sea-land
interface), but should also include changes in the dune/beach, as well as the nearshore
topography. For this purpose both land and nearshore topographic measurements are required
on a regular basis (extended hydrographic survey area). A part of these monitoring activities are
already included in ongoing monitoring programs.
Maintenance dredging and beneficial usage of dredged sediments
Regular monitoring is required with respect to changes in sedimentation in the navigational
channel and the northern harbor part, to study the effects of the project on maintenance
dredging. The resulting information is to include information on the characteristics of the
sediments (type of sediment, grain size distribution and level of pollution) in view of possible
beneficial usage. The data should be stored in a so-called "Nautical and Environmental database
system. Background information on the N&EDS is presented in section 8.5.1.
The proposed monitoring activities are part of the normal maintenance dredging related
activities, which may need to be adjusted to fulfill the present and future needs.
8.4.2  MONITORING RELATED TO THE CONSTRUCTION ACTIVITIES OF THE PROJECT
Increased levels of suspended sediments - turbidity
Resuspension and dispersion of fine sediments will take place during dredging operations and
during placement of the construction materials. In view of fish migration and nearby spawning
areas monitoring of this aspect is required.
The resulting information should indicate the scale of resuspension for the various types of
dredgers and auxiliary equipment, the various types of sediment or construction materials, as
well as the dispersion in time and place. Based on the monitoring information additional
mitigating measures may be developed if and when required.
Fish migration and spawning during the construction and dredging works is to be monitored as
well. The key parameters for fish migration should include: type of species, migration routes and
migration intensity. For fish spawning the key parameters should include: spawning locations,
timing and duration of spawning, period till hatching, spreading of fry, temperature and
suspended sediment levels.
Dredging contaminated sediments
In case contaminated sediments are to be dredged, the relevant characteristics of this type of
dredging should be monitored, e.g. accuracy of dredging, turbidity and spillage. The resulting
information should indicate differences between the design level and the dredged level in
centimeters.
Offshore disposal
To ensure that dredged sediments are only dumped at the designated offshore disposal site,
control monitoring is required. For this purpose the equipment to be used for transporting the
sediments to the offshore disposal site should be equipped with:
*  a GPS-positioning system (or better)
*  a PC and related software to record: date, time, position, and load information (based on
depth gauges of the barge/transport-ship).
H7371   Draft Environmental Impact Assessment  8-10                            September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                          S
HARRIS
Beach or foreshore replenishment
To ensure that only sand and no silt and clayballs are placed on the beach, the dredging
contractor should carefully monitor the loading process during dredging. Each load should be
judged individually in order to assess if the load is suitable for beach replenishment, for
nearshore replenishment or should go to the offshore disposal site.
Anti-pollution program
To ensure compliance with the anti-pollution program as is to be presented by the contractor,
control monitoring in the form of independent incidental audits during and after completion of the
works are required. Items to be included in the control monitoring are: fuel bunkering, waste
handling, storage facilities and construction facilities.
8.4.3  MANAGEMENT AND EXECUTION OF THE MONITORING PROGRAMS
As the owner of the project, the Port Authorities are responsible for monitoring the design
consequences of the project (operational phase). These monitoring activities, which will cover a
period of at least 2 to 10 years after the works have been completed, include:
*  Reduction of hydraulic resistance and related effects
*  Changes in coastline development
* Changes in maintenance dredging volumes
As parts of these monitoring activities are already elements of ongoing monitoring programs, it is
recommended that the KSSA will work out detailed monitoring programs for these items, in close
co-operation with the involved third parties.
In view of the KSSA's direct involvement into the project, it is recommended that an independent
monitoring authority is appointed to oversee and conduct monitoring related to the construction
activities. The 'Construction Supervision Team (CST)" to be appointed for the execution of the
works, is proposed to be this independent monitoring agency for the following reasons:
* The CST has a clear task and commitment to ensure the works are undertaken according
the contract and the EMP.
* The CST has a clear view on project planning as well as on the daily activities, which
facilitates planning of the monitoring activities.
* In view of its role, the CST has direct and open communication lines with both the Project
Implementation Unit (PIU) and the Contractor. This greatly facilitates quick response actions
when required in case of non compliance with the contract or the EMP.
* The CST is directly involved in technical monitoring, like production processes and work
progress. Items that are directly related to the environmental monitoring program, like
turbidity control.
It is foreseen that for specific monitoring activities, like fish migration, fish spawning and other
field measurements, the CST will be assisted by experts from Lithuanian institutes, e.g. the
Klaipeda University, the Marine Research Center, The Fishery Research Laboratory, the
Institute of Geography and the Vilnius University.
Based on the planning and the work methods of the contractor, and in line with the items
presented in section 8.4.2 of this EMP, the CST is to work out a detailed works program for the
environmental monitoring activities. This works program is to include the monitoring topics, the
monitoring strategy, timing, frequency of measuwements, people and equipment involved, as well
as costs involved. The monitoring works program is to be completed before the start of the
execution of the works.

8.5  ADDITIONAL WORKS
In this section additional works directly related to the project are identified. Included are:
* Set-up of a database system for dredging and environmental data (8.5.1)
* A contaminated sediment remediation program (8.5.2)
* The design and implementation of a CDF for contaminated sediments (8.5.3)
8.5.1  DATABASE SYSTEM FOR NAUTICAL AN2D NKVIRONMENTAL DATA
The data and information which had to be collected for this World Bank project, included a
variety of environmental and dredging related data, e.g. bottom topography, sediment
composition, layer thickness, levels of contamination, water quality characteristics, dredged
areas, dredged volumes and characteristics, hydrographic survey data, salinity data, levels of
suspended sediments, fishery data, etc.
Although quite some information was known to exist, it was sometimes very hard or even
impossible to get the data made available to the study team. Although several earlier studies
were carried out on behalf of the Port Authorities, most of the information and data was only
available from the original source (private company, public organization or University experts).
Besides the information was fragmented, incomplete and sometimes incompatible. Data on
levels of sediment contamination were considered "Classified" and only a part of the information
could be bought from the original sources; often after several months of requesting.
This situation is a clear disadvantage to the Port Authorities, being the manager of the entire
Klaipeda port area. Not only has it caused considerable delays to the World bank project, but the
lack of a central knowledge base, or "Nautical and Environmental Database System" (N&EDS),
hampers proper planning of future development projects. With respect to the wish of Lithuania to
become part of the European Community, it is to be noted that the present situation is not in line
with the 1990 EC Directive on freedom of access to information on the environment.
It is clear that information availability can be improved by creating a N&EDS for the Port
Authorities. By storing and analyzing nautical and environmental information, future works and
activities of the Port Authorities can be better planned, e.g. maintenance dredging, beneficial
usage of dredged sediments, contaminated sediment problems, coastal erosion problems, etc.
Besides, by making data and information free and easy accessible to third parties, the data and
information can also be used for other then their original purpose, e.g. coastal zone
management, fishery research, education, in-house training, marketing, etc.
The N&EDS should be PC based and should include so-called GIS (Geographical Information
System) software. In this way data can be presented on standard maps and charts. The retrieval
of information and knowledge should be facilitated by use of simple metadata records accessible
through Internet-based gateways.
Although developed with and for the Port Authorities, the N&EDS should also be promoted and
developed in close co-operation with other possible end-users, especially University experts.
This to ensure that the results from research projects, surveys and monitoring activities will find
their way into the database system as well.
The development of the N&EDS, including the purchase of hardware and software, the design of
the database structure, implementation, testing and training, reporting and external consultancy,
is estimated at approximately 150,000 US$.
H7371   Draft Environmental Impact Assessment  8-13                            September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                        HARRIS
8.5.2  A CONTAMINATED SEDIMENT REMEDIATION PROGRAM
A serious problem with respect to the contaminated sediment issue and consequently with
planning of the capacity of a CDF (Confined Disposal Facility) is the fact that there are no
accurate data available regarding the volumes of contaminated sediment present, the variations
in layer thickness, the toxicity of the contaminated sediments, dredgeability and effects of
dredging tolerances on dredged volumes, treatment options to minimize the volumes to be
stored. etc.
To fill this information gap, a remediation program is highly recommended. This program should
preferably be carried out as a joint effort by the Worldbank study team and Lithuanian experts.
The total costs of the program, including limited field sampling and laboratory analyses are
estimated at approximately 200.000 US$.
Background information on presence of contaminated sediments
In 1995 (Haskoning study) the total volume of contaminated sediments in the Klaipeda port
areas was estimated at approximately 365.000 m3.
In the summer of 1998 the Geographical Institute in Vilnius (Lithuania) executed an extensive
investigation on the presence of contaminants throughout the port of Klaipeda. Sediment
samples were taken in 192 positions from the port entrance up to and including Malku Bay.
Samples were taken by using a Van Veen grab and a drop corer. The results of the
investigations have been reported separately (Geographical Institute, 1998) and have also been
used in a preliminary report to the implementation of a confined disposal facility (Association of
Lithuanian Hydrobiologists, 1999). The results of the investigations shows that most of the
contaminated areas are related to the presence of silty sediments. The assessed quantities of
contaminated sediments are summarized in Table 8-1.
Table 8-1
Contaminated sediment in Klaipeda Port
Class               % of silty  In situ quantity   Area  Average layer thickness
sediments       mi3         (kr2)             (cm)
i  Clean               4               31,000   0.6                5
II  Little polluted    36             271,000   2.5                10
iII  Polluted          58             437,000    1.1               40
IV  Highly polluted     2              13,000   0.05               25
Total             100              13,000   0.05               25
Source: Treatment site for contaminated sediments from the water territory of Klaipeda Port. (Association of
Lithuanian Hydrobiologists, 1999)
Looking at the distribution of these sediments (figure 8-2) it is observed that most of the port's
fairway is contaminated with Class II sediment, whereas Class IlIl and Class IV contaminated
sediments are found along most of the quays and in inner harbors (Winter port, Malku bay).
Implicitly this means that any expansion or rehabilitation of the existing quay structures requiring
deepening in front of the quays, requires Class IlIl and/or Class IV sediments to be dredged.
According Lithuanian guidelines these materials can not be dumped in open sea. The
aforementioned studies emphasize the findings of the EIA that for the future planning and
progress of the port a Confined Dispqsal Facility for environmentally safe storage of
contaminated sediments is urgently required.

Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                       NRI
The Lithuanian experts of the Association of Hydrobiologists indicate in their report that in some
cases Class IlIl sediments are overlyinglayers of Class II contaminated sediments. Theoretically
it is assessed that the actual quantity of Class IlIl contaminated sediments includes some
201,000 m3. However, taking into account the available dredging techniques it is concluded not
possible to dredge with the required accuracy. Hence the total quantity of contaminated
sediment required to be stored or treated is estimated at 450,000 m3.
Consultants would like to indicate that present day's dredging techniques manage to maintain a
vertical accuracy of 0.10 m, when using advanced dredging equipment (with respect to
horizontal and vertical dredging control) and a trained crew. However, for the quantities indicated
Consultants assess it to be more realistic to apply a dredging tolerance of 0.20 m. Adopting the
Class Ill layer to have an average thickness of 0.20 m thick (=201,000 m3/1.1 k Mn2), it will be
required that such layer is dredged with a thickness of 0.30 m (to make sure all contaminated
sediments will be dredged). Taking into account a practical dredging tolerance of 20 cm, the
amount of sediment dredged including the layer of contaminated sediments would be around
550,000 m3. For the Class IV sediments, with an average layer thickness of 0.25 m, because of
dredging requirements the amount of dredged sediments would be around 27,500 m3. As a
result of this, the amount of in situ dredged contaminated sediments to be stored in a Confined
Disposal Facility is assessed at 577,500 m3, which leads to a minimal 600,000 m3 storage
volume in a Confined Disposal Facility.
In addition to this amount of contaminated sediment to be stored to re-mediate the present day
contaminated sediment problems of the port, a reservation has to be made for the future
maintenance dredging in the port as well. Lithuanian experts assess the amount of silty
sediments to be deposited annually at 100,000 m3. Based on the area distribution of
contaminated silty sediments, it is assessed that initially 34,000 m3 of Class III/IV material will be
deposited each year. However, when sources of pollution will be re-mediated in due course this
amount of contaminated maintenance dredging will be reduced as well, for which argument
Consultants assume the annual contaminated maintenance dredging to be some 20,000 m3 for
the coming 10 years. Hence the required size of a Confined Disposal Facility to solve the
contaminated sediment problems for the port of Klaipeda in the coming 10 years is 800,000 m3.
A storage amount of 800,000 m3 is a considerable amount and reduction of this quantity may be
looked for in the following areas:
Precisely identifying the layers of contaminated sediment. Presently some 200 samples have
been taken throughout the port to identify the contaminated sediment problem. By precisely
indicating (vertically and horizontally) where Class I to Class IV contaminated sediment can be
found, not only a detailed estimate of the quantity of contaminated sediments can be obtained,
but also a detailed dredging plan can made where to dredge which layers to what depth.
By minimizing the inclusion of clean or lightly contaminated sediments (due to over-dredging and
dredging tolerances), the indicated amount will be reduced. However, increasing the accuracy of
dredging and reducing the dredging tolerances will put a larger demand on the dredging
capabilities (equipment and staff) of a dredging contractor, resulting in increased dredging cost.
The effect of bulking of sediments (increasing volume as a consequence of handling) is not yet
taken into consideration, as filling of the CDF is expected to take place gradually during the
years. Settlement and compaction of the sediments inside the CDF will strongly reduce the
bulking effect caused by handling.  -  -
Separation of clean sand and contaminated silts can reduce the quantity of contaminated
sediments to be used. Generally, with more than 50% sands in the dredged spoil, separation of
sand and silt will lead to a reduction of the quantity to be stored. However, with less than 50%
H7371   Draft Environmental Impact Assessment  8-16                          September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                      HARRIS
sand in the dredged spoil, the quantity to be stored does not reduce due to the adverse
dewatering characteristics of the remaining silt-water mixture.
Treatment of the sediments in the form of cleaning (removal or destruction of contaminants) may
result in a very large reduction of the quantity of sediments to be stored.
It goes without saying that reduction of the total quantity of contaminated sediments to be stored
does have its price. Which options can be used will have to be studied in more detail as part of
the remediation program, which in itself can be included in the CDF study.
Overview of finalized, ongoing and planned capital and maintenance dredging works
On additional problem in relation to proper planning of the required CDF capacity is the ongoing
removal of contaminated sediments from various parts of the port and its subsequent dumping
at the offshore disposal site. A summary of the finalized, ongoing and planned dredging works
inside the Port of Klaipeda is presented in tables 8-2, 8-3 and 8-4.
It is noted that a considerable number of capital dredging works is planned for the period
from the present to 2003. Practically all of these projects will involve dredging of
contaminated sediments. The present plans to implement a CDF after all of these works
have been completed is like putting the cart before the horse. It is therefore highly
recommended to expedite the implementation of a CDF and to postpone all dredging
works in contaminated areas till a CDF has become available.
