8.5.3  CONFINED DISPOSAL FACILITY FOR CONTAMINATED SEDIMENTS
INTRODUCTION
With part of the bottom sediments in Klaipeda port being too contaminated to be dumped
offshore, the dredging and disposal of these contaminated sediments forms a regularly recurring
problem. To solve this problem, this EIA describes a so-called "Preferred Alternative", which
includes the storage of contaminated sediments in a Confinmd Disposal Facility (CDF).
In view of the planned capital dredging projects under the investment program for Klaipeda Port,
it is highly recommended to expedite the implementation of a CDF and to postpone all dredging
works in contaminated areas till a CDF has become available.
In this section some concepts of a Confined Disposal Facility to store contaminated sediments
from the Klaipeda port are being discussed. Two of these concepts have been developed by
Haskoning in 1995 and two other concepts have been identified by the Consultants within the
present study. For all concepts a first order cost estimate for the implementation costs have
been provided. Recommendations for the further design and construction of such CDF, including
detailed cost estimates for implementation, are provided.
LOCATIONS
When deciding on the implementation of a CDF, an important issue to take into account is the
location of the CDF to be constructed. The HASKONING study resulted in a preliminary design and
a preliminary environmental impact study for two possible disposal sites: the Ship Cemetery and
the Dreverna site:
The Ship Cemeterv:
The Ship Cemetery is located along the Klaipeda Port fairway at approx. location 55040.8' N,
21008.1' E (Fig. 8-3). With the depth of the fairway locally being nearly 9 m, due to its location
the site is easily accessible for dredges and
barges. Further, the disposal site is located
approximately in the middle of the port and thus
in the heart of the contaminated sediment  Sea Museum CDF             KLAIPEDA CITY
problem. The resulting short transport distances    Cr S
will be  beneficial  for  the  execution  of   Curonian Spit CDF Q
contaminated sediment dredging and disposal.  Ship Cemetery \OF
The Dreverna site:
The Dreverna site is not as well defined in
location as the Ship Cemetery, but has roughly
been indicated between 5534' N and 5536.5' N
on the eastern shore of the Kursiu Lagoon (Fig.
8-3). This  results  in  considerable  sailing  . Sea
distances (order of 10 to 15 km) from the areas                            Drevema CDF
where the contaminated sediments are to be
dredged. Second disadvantage about the location
is the rather shallow depth in the Kursiu Lagoon.

Lagoon
Figure 8-3: Locations of CDF's (indicative)
H7371   Draft Environmental Impact Assessment  8-19                            September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                         ARRIS
HARI
In the execution of this EIA, Consultants identified two alternatives for a CDF. One of these is
located behind the Sea Museum, taking advantage of an already present basin. The other exact
location for a CDF still has to be specified. Requirement for this last location would be that the
glacial till bottom layer should be quite near to the ground surface. According the soils
investigations carried out for the project, this layer can be found at a depth of approximately -12
m CD under the Curonian Spit. In short these two sites can be described as:
The Sea Museum site:
The Sea Museum site is located at approx. 55043.2' N, 21006.2' E (Fig. 8-3). The site is located
close to the fairway through Klaipeda port and with the depth locally being nearly 12 m, easy
accessible for dredges and barges. The sailing distances to the locations with contaminated
sediment are in the order of 2.5 to 8.5 km.
The Curonian Spit site:
The Curonian Spit site is not as well defined as the Sea Museum site, but is roughly proposed to
be located between the Ship Cemetery site and the Sea Museum site. This puts the site close to
the fairway with sufficient depth for dredges and barges. Further, also the sailing distances to
the dredge areas with contaminated sediments are short (order of 5 km).
It is emphasized that in proposing three potential locations of a CDF on the Curonian Spit, it has
not been overlooked that the Curonian Spit is a National Park. However, when it is considered
that a CDF is essentially a closed system from which contaminants are not supposed to leak, the
proposals do have some specific advantages:
1.    With large scale infrastructural and urban developments not allowed in the National
Park, it will be very unlikely that the CDF will ever be in the way of any future
developments, as it might be when located near urban Klaipeda.
2.    The long term after care of a CDF constructed in the National Park could fall under the
obligations of the organization maintaining the National Park. This organization, in itself
concerned with the care for nature, should understand the importance of the CDF and
take proper care of it.
3.    It being a NATIONAL park, a clear directive from the National Government (i.e. the
Ministry of Environment) can overrule the well known Not-In-My-Backyard attitude to the
implementation to the CDF. Clearly, the Ministry of Environment has to be convinced of
the advantages of having the CDF on the Curonian Spit
4.     Once filled, capped and completed, the CDF can be properly embedded in the natural
environment of the National Park.
Finally it is observed that at the Northern part of the Curonian Spit a lot of activities take place,
such as: presence of quays of ferry links, museums, houses, Coast Guard station. In view of
this, it is not considered a loss for the park if a well functioning disposal site is created here.
Still, the above sites are identified as being potential sites. The feasibility of these sites has not
been demonstrated yet, let alone that approvals to construct a CDF at one (or more) of these
sites have been received. Prior to the design and construction of a CDF at any of these site a
detailed feasibility study to the (final) location of the CDF will be required.
STORAGE CAPACITY
The storage capacity of the Ship Cemetery site and the Sea Museum site have been assessed
at:
*  Ship Cemetery:   85,000 m3 volume corresponding to 65,000 m3 in situ dredge sludge
*  Sea Museum:      60,000 m3 volume corresponding to 45,000 m3 in situ dredge sludge
In view of these relatively small capacities, these sites may be considered as temporary disposal
facilities. As final CDF's these sites might be attractive when the amounts of contaminated
H7371   Draft Environmental Impact Assessment  8-20                            September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                            lRI
HARRIS
sediment to be stored in the depots can be reduced. Some of these techniques are indicated in
section 8.5.2, but in the following these have not been taken into account.
The storage capacity for the Dreverna site and Curonian Spit site are much larger, as both sites
are supposedly to provide a long term solution to the contaminated sediments problem of the
port of Klaipeda. The storage capacity for these sites have been assessed at:
*  Dreverna site:    500,000 m3 volume corresponding to 350,000 m3 in situ dredge sludge
* Curonian spit site: in view of the uncertainties about the quantities of contaminated
sediment still present in Klaipeda Port, a CDF with 200,000 m3, 400,000 m3 and 600,000 m3
has been identified, respectively for 150,000 m3, 300,000 m3 and 450,000 m3 of in situ
dredge spoil
It is clear that the storage capacity of the CDF will strongly affect the costs of implementation. At
present, based on the most recently available information it is assessed that in the port of
Klaipeda still some 200,000 to 450,000 m3 of contaminated sediment remain (depending on
dredgeability and dredging tolerances). To this amount an extra 20,000 m3 per year may have to
be added for extra contaminated sediment to be formed in the years ahead.
CONSTRUCTION
The construction/design concepts of the Confined Disposal Facilities at the aforementioned of
the sites are described as follows:
ShiD Cemetery site:
The disposal of spoil at the Ship Cemetery site will take place in water as well as on land. The
boundaries of the site are the existing slopes and a sheetpile dam, which is still to be
constructed. The latter functions as a retaining structure and separates the spoil from Klaipeda
Strait. The isolation of the contaminated sediments at this site is obtained partly by physical
barriers (e.g. sheetpile dam, sand-bentonite, HDPE-liner, soil capping) and partly by
geohydrological isolation (i.e. groundwater abstraction). The top and bottom drainage systems
ensure removal of excess water. This concerns consolidation water, ground water, rainfall and
water which was added during the excavation and transport process. The contaminated water is
discharged to a water treatment plant with a capacity of 30 m3/hour.
Dreverna site:
The disposal of spoil at the Dreverna site will take place on land. The contaminated sediments
are isolated using earth dams (spatial isolation from the sides) along the rectangular perimeter,
sand-bentonite from below, and a capping consisting of a drainage layer and a soil layer. Also in
this site safe removal of contaminated water is ensured using a top and bottom drainage system
and a waste water treatment plant with a capacity of 35 m3/hour.
The other two disposal facilities can be described as follows:
The Sea Museum site:
The disposal of spoil at the Sea Museum site will take place on land in an existing basin (Figure
8-4). The contaminated sediments are isolated using earth dams covered with concrete
(existing) along the rectangular perimeter. Crevices in the existing concrete cover are to be filled
with non-shrink grout or other sealing material. The same isolation is applied at the bottom of the
site. At the top a capping consisting of a drainage layer and a soil layer is to be provided. Similar
as for the other side a top and bottom drainage system is to be provided and a water treatment
plant with a capacity of about 30 m3/hour.

Similar as for the other sites a top and bottom drainage system is to be provided and a water

ENVIRONMENTAL IMPACT ASSESSMENT
Adopting that the isolating measures, after care and monitoring program for the CDF function
properly, it is assessed that the impacts of the mere CDF to the environment will be minimal,
provided that efforts are made to integrate the CDF in its natural environment.
In that respect, Consultants observe that the construction height of the Ship Cemetery and
Dreverna sites are considerable (6 to 8 m above existing ground level). Especially at the
Dreverna site integration into the (flat) natural environment would be difficult.

emphasized that the costs for dredging, transport and disposal of the contaminated sediment is
not being included in these estimates, since for the major CDF's (Dreverna site and Curonian
Spit site) the exact transport distances are unknown.

CONCLUSIONS AND RECOMMENDATIONS
One of the main conclusions of this EIA is that the design and construction of a CDF is urgently
required if the port of Klaipeda is to carry out maintenance dredging and capital dredging inside
the port in accordance with national and international guidelines for the preservation of nature.
Based on the 1998 field investigations on contaminated sediments still present in the port,
Lithuanian experts estimate the amount-of level IlIl and IV contaminated sediments inside the
port to be 215,000 m3 minimum  up to 440,000 m3 maximum. The actual amount actually
depends on possibility to differentiate (vertically) during dredging operations between level 11 and
level IlIl contaminated sediments. Yearly 100,000 m3 of fresh silt will be deposited in the harbor.
How much of this 100,000 m3 of silt is contaminated is not quite clear.
)
H7371    Oratt Environmental Impact Assessment  8-23                              September 1999



Klaipeda Port Entrance Rehabilitation Project                                             HARRIS
When considering the implementation of a CDF, it will be clear that a small CDF will not be
sufficient. The capacity of both the Ship Cemetery Site and Sea Museum site are insufficient to
store all the contaminated materials present.
When considering the storage of existing and anticipated contaminated sediment for another 10
years to come, the storage capacity required may be as much as 800,000 m3. Methods to
reduce the volume of contaminated sediments will have to be studied as part the design of the
CDF.
With the requirements for the implementation of a CDF (again) clearly demonstrated in this EIA
and the impact which a delay in the implementation may have on the development plans of the
Port of Klaipeda, it will be clear that a fast start up of the design and construction of a CDF is to
be promoted by all parties involved: KSSA, Ministry of Transport and Ministry of Environment.

Law on Environmental Impact Assessment of                               pagma I van 0
Law on Environmental Impact Assessment of
the Republic of Lithuania
adopted on August 15, 1996
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL PROVISIONS
Article 1. Definitions
Environment means a system of interdependent elements (surface, ground, air, water, soil, fauna,
flora, organic and inorganic matter, and human beings) functioning in nature as well as natural
and anthropogenic systems unifying these elements.
Environmental impact means a probable change in environment caused by a proposed activity.
Environmental impact assessment means the process of identifying and predicting the potential
impact of a proposed activity on the environment.
Special planning provisions mean provisions which set the special requirements of governmental
institutions and institutions of local government, in case there are no appropriate normative
documents, or the requirements depend on the environment of the construction site.
Program of the environmental impact assessment means a document which determines the scope
and contents of the environmental impact assessment process.
Environmental impact assessment report means a document which presents the results of the
undertaken environmental impact assessment and is prepared in accordance with the
environmental impact assessment program.
Proposed activity means the future activity (objects of construction or reconstruction) or foreseen
changes in ongoing activity (modernization, reprofile of production, implementation of new
production in existing buildings) which may affect the environment.
Decision on the physical planning documentation means a consequence of a decision on the
physical planning tasks, represented in written or graphical form and defining nature, conditions
and order for management and development of territories, land plots or their groups.
Project proposals mean the initial stage of a construction project preparation, during which the
main data concerning local conditions, proposed activity and potential impacts on environment is
provided.
State Expertise of Environmental Impact Assessment means an extensive verification of the
adequateness of the environmental impact assessment which has been conducted by the
proponent. The state expertise is organized by the specially empowered governmental body -
Ministry of Environmental Protection, together with licensed experts.
Article 2 Aim of the Law
http://H95.182.68.5/Povapl/T_aktai/Ang/Law_EIA.html                            2-9-98



Law on Environmental Impact Assessment of                                 pagina 2 van 6
The aim of the Law on environmental impact assessment, is to provide regulations for the
evaluation of a proposed activity which may cause negative impact on the environment and also to
regulate relationships between parties involved in the process.
Article 3. Aims of the environmental impact assessment
The aim of the initial environmental impact assessment is the preliminary finding if the proposed
activity may be carried out in the chosen site.
The aim of the full environmental impact assessment is to identify all potential effects on the
environment caused by a proposed activity, to assess the social aspects of the proposed activity,
and to provide mitigation measures.
Article 4. Legal basis for the environmental impact assessment
Legal basis for the environmental impact assessment is this Law, the Law on Environmental
Protection of the Republic of Lithuania, the Law on Territorial Planning as well as other laws and
legal acts providing regulations for use of natural resources and environmental protection.
Article 5. Object of the environmental impact assessment
Object of the environmental impact assessment is the proposed activity which may cause direct or
indirect negative effect on the environment.
Article 6. Participants of the environmental impact assessment process
Participants of the environrmental impact assessment process are:
1. Relevant parties of the environmental impact assessment of a proposed activity are:
a) proponents of a proposed activity and organizations of physical planning;
b) Ministry of Environmental Protection;
c) Ministry of Health Protection;
d) Fire Protection Department of the Ministry of Domestic Affairs;
e) regional administration;
f) municipal administration;
2. Public.
CHAPTER 2
THE ENVIRONMENTAL IMPACT ASSESSMENT PROCEDURE
Article 7. Stages of the environmental impact assessment
1. Environmental impact assessment consists of the following stages:
http://l 95.182.68.5/Povapl/T_aktai/Ang/Law_EIA.html                             2-9-98



Law on Envirornental impact Assessment of                                  pagina 3 van 6
1) initial EIA, performed in the process of preparation of documents on territorial planning and
project proposals;
2) full EIA, performed in the process of preparation of technical projects.
2. Initial environmental impact assessment is performed investigating:
1) all documents of territorial planning, and assessing the consequences of decisions by the special
orders prepared and adopted by the Government;
2) projects proposals of a proposed activity.
3. Initial environmental impact assessment is to be performed by the proponent according to the
special provisions of the territory and construction planning and given by the relevant parties of
EIA.
4. Results of the environmental impact assessment are to be included into the documents on
territorial planning and/or project proposals which will then be presented to the relevant parties of
EIA for the decision. The proponent shall also present the before- mentioned documents to the
public and summarize its comments.
5. The Ministry of Environment Protection, together with other relevant parties of EIA shall then
make the decision, taking into account the results of initial EIA as well as conclusions and
comments of other relevant institutions.
6. Full environmental impact assessment is to be performed for the proposed activities and objects
which are included into the list prepared by the Ministry of Environmental Protection and adopted
by the Government of the Republic of Lithuania.
7. All the participants of the EIA process are entitled to require, and the Ministry of
Environmental Protection to take a decision that the full environmental impact assessment is
performed also for a proposed activity not included into the list, if the preliminary environmental
impact assessment shows that the proposed activity will have a significant effect on the
environment and this effect can be evaluated only performing the full environmental impact
assessment.
8. The proponent then performs the full EIA, according to the program and prepares a report.
Article 8. Preparation of the environmental impact assessment program
The full environmental impact assessment program, including consideration of alternatives, is
prepared in accordance with special regulations issued and approved by the Ministry of
Environmental Protection.
The proponent submits the environmental impact assessment program to the relevant parties of
environrmental impact assessment for approval and presents the program to the public. The
proponent takes into account the public comments and then submits the program to the Ministry
of Environmental Protection for ratification.
Article 9. Preparation of the environmental impact assessment report
http://195.182.68.5/Povapl/T_aktai/Ang/Law_EIA.html                               2-9-98



Law on Environmental Impact Assessment of                                pagina 4 van 6
Under the environmental impact assessment program the proponent must identify the potential
effect of the proposed activity on the environment, provide prevention or mitigation measures, and
prepare the report of the full environmental impact assessment.
The proponent submits the environmental impact assessment report to the relevant parties of
environmental impact assessment for approval. The relevant parties of EIA are responsible for
their conclusions in accordance with their competence.
The proponent presents the environmental impact assessment report to the public.
Article 10. Procedure of the full environmental impact assessment report review
The relevant parties of EIA, within their competence, check whether the full environmental
impact assessment report meets requirements of the adopted program, if the effects on the
environment caused by a proposed activity meet existing environmental standards, limits and
other requirements, and in the time period of one month forward the conclusions to the proponent.
The proponent submits the full environmental impact assessment report to the Ministry of
Environmental Protection, together with conclusions issued by other relevant parties of the
environmental impact assessment and with the analysis of public comments.
The Ministry of Environrnental Protection examines the EIA report and considers the conclusions
issued by other institutions that have also examined the report. The Ministry of Environmental
Protection shall then decide, in the time period of one month, if the proposed mitigation measures
are adequate to ensure the quality of environment according to the existing environmental
standards. The Ministry of Environmental Protection shall forward its decision and reasonings to
the proponent in written form.
The Ministry of Environmental Protection shall make a decision concerning the proposed activity
for which the State Expertize on EIA is mandatory only if the SE procedure has been performed.
Article 11. State expertise of the environmental impact assessment
State expertise of the environmental impact assessment is obligatory for the proposed activities
and objects included into the list which is prepared by the Ministry of Environmental Protection
and adopted by the Government of the Republic of Lithuania.
State expertise of the environmental impact assessment may be performed only by the licensed
EIA experts.
The license of an EIA expert is given according to the regulations adopted by the Government of
the Republic of Lithuania.
State expertise of the environmental impact assessment is organized by the Ministry of
Environmental Protection:
1) the program of the state expertise of EIA is prepared together with the relevant parties of EIA
and the experts are selected on a competition basis;
} 2) the Ministry of Environmental Protection and the experts prepare the agreement on the
performance of the state expertise of the environmental impact assessment;
http://l 95.182.68.5/PovapU/T_aktai/Ang/Law_EIA.html                           2-9-98



Law on Envirornental Impact Assessment of                                pagina 5 van 6
3) the estimate of expenditures and time-table are to be prepared and approved by the Ministry of
Environmental Protection and the proponent;
4) the costs of the state expertise of the environmental impact assessment are to be paid by the
proponent of a proposed activity;
5) the experts submit their conclusions to the Ministry of Environmental Protection and are
responsible for their truthfulness;
6) the Ministry of Environmental Protection summarizes the conclusions of experts and forward
them to the proponent, which has to take them into account;
7) fulfillment of the conclusions of the state expertise of the environmental impact assessment is
controlled by the Ministry of Environmental Protection, which makes the final decision
concerning the proposed activity.
5. The state expertise of the environmental impact assessment is a component of the combined
state project expertise.
CHAPTER 3
FINAL STATEMENTS
Article 12. Publicity of the process of the environmental impact assessment
The public has a right to obtain information about the going-on environmental impact assessment
from the project proponent and to express proposals, comments and claims. The proponent of the
proposed activity must consider the public comments and motivate the decision.
The public participation in the process of the initial EIA is organized by the institutions of local
government;
The proponent must organize a public discussion on the results of the environmental impact
assessment. Costs of the discussion shall be paid by the proponent.
Regulations for public participation in the process of the environmental impact assessment are to
be adopted by the Government of the Republic of Lithuania.
Article 13. Validity of the conclusions of the environmental impact assessment
Conclusions on the proposed activity are valid for three years after they are issued.
The proposed activity cannot be carried out if the EIA decision made by the Ministry of
Environmental Protection is negative.
Article 14. Investigation of disputes
Disputes concerning the enforcement of this Law are investigated by the Courts of the Republic of
Lithuania according to the currently established order.
Disputes between the Republic of Lithuania and legal or physical bodies of the foreign countries
http://195.182.68.5/Povapl/T_aktai/Ang/Law._EIA.html                            2-9-98



Law on Environmental Impact Assessment of                              pagina 6 van 6
are investigated according to the laws of the Republic of Lithuania, if the international
conventions, signed by the Republic of Lithuania, do not provide different regulations.
http:H/1 95.1 82.68.5/Povapl/T_aktai/Ang/Law_EIA.html                         2-9-98

The order of informing the public about the proposed activity
and implementing the proposals of the public
General provisions
l. This order shall regulate the stages and procedures of the public discussions of the full
environmental impact assessment findings, ensure the publicity of the assessment, provide a
possibility for the community members to participate in the full environmental impact assessment
process, to achieve the goals set by the Law on Environmental Impact Assessment of the Republic
of Lithuania.
2. Public discussion is a compulsory constituent part of the full environmental impact assessment
process.
The list of the categories of proposed activities and projects that shall be made subject to the full
environmental impact assessment is approved by the Government of the Republic of Lithuania.
3. This order shall be binding for all relevant parties (subjects) of the environmental impact
assessment (governmental and municipal institutions, other physical persons and legal entities).
http://1 95.182.68.5/Povapl/T aktai/Ang/info.html                               2-9-98



Unofficial translation by Mindaugas Raulinaitis                             pagina 2 van 3
Stages and procedures of the public discussions of the findings
of full environmental impact assessment
Stages of the public discussions of the findings
4. The findings of full environmental impact assessment are publicly discussed in two stages:
4.1. The first stage - consideration of the full environmental impact assessment program (EIA
program), which determines the scope and contents of the environmental impact assessment
process;
4.2. The second stage - consideration of the full environmental impact assessment report, which
has been prepared in accordance with the EIA program.
The first stage
5. The public shall be informed about the public discussions of the full environmental impact
assessment:
5.1. if the proposed activity is of national importance or may have an effect on all members of the
community of Lithuania - on the Lithuanian radio and television, in the press (including local
press), via advertisements in the administrative buildings of the counties and municipal
institutions;
5.2. if the proposed activity is of local importance and may have an effect only on the members of
the local district's community - via local mass media, via advertisements in the administrative
buildings of the local district.
6. After the EIA program is prepared and ratified by the relevant parties (subjects) of the
environmental impact assessment, the proponent shall employ the announcement methods,
pursuant to paragraph 5, and provide the following information no later than 20 days before the
public discussion:
6.1. when and where the discussion will take place, when and where it is possible to get
acquainted with the EIA program. The discussion shall take place in the territory of the proposed
activity and at the time convenient for the public (not during the working hours);
6.2. when, in what way, in what time period, and to whom the proposals may be submitted.
7. In order to submit the proposals on the EIA program amendment, the governmental institutions,
public organizations, other physical persons and legal entities, which are not the relevant parties
(subjects) of the environmental impact assessment shall indicate their place of residence (the
name of the organization), name, surname, address, and date.
8. Participants of the discussion are registered by a registrar, appointed by the proponent. The
signatures of the participants shall be used in order to register. The discussion shall be chaired by
the proponent, or by the preparer of the EIA program, authorized by the proponent. The secretary
of the discussion shall be appointed by the proponent. The speeches of the participants shall be
http://195.182.68.5/Povapl/T_aktai/Ang/info.html                                   2-9-9S



Unofficial translation by Mindaugas Raulinaitis                               pagina 3 van 3
recorded in the minutes. The minutes of the discussion shall be signed by the chairman, the
secretary, and the representative of the public, who shall be elected by the participants of the
discussion.
If in one hour after the appointed beginning of the discussion there are no participants present, the
registrar may state that the discussion did not take place. This statement shall be recorded in the
minutes and signed by the proponent and the registrar.
9. During the discussion, the proponent or the preparer of the EIA program, authorized by the
proponent, defines the nature of the proposed activity, describes the EIA program, answers the
questions of the participants, and evaluates the proposals of the public. The proposals are to be
submitted in written form before the beginning of the discussion. If the author of the proposal is
absent, or if there are new proposals arisen during the discussion, the proponent shall inform the
author about his decision in written form, providing the reasons on which the decision is based.
The proponent shall inform the author no later than in 10 days after the public discussion.
During the discussion, the information regarding the second stage of the public discussion shall be
presented. The second stage of the discussion shall take place after the EIA report is prepared
according to the EIA program.
10. After the discussion, the proponent together with the preparer of the EIA program shall
analyze and evaluate the proposals of the public.
The EIA program shall be submitted to the Environmental Protection Ministry for ratification.
The conclusions of the public proposals analysis, the minutes of the discussion, and the list of
participants shall be submitted to the Environmental Protection Ministry as well. If there are no
public proposals or if there were no participants present, the proponent shall submit the minutes
which inform that the discussion did not take place.
The second stage
11. After the EIA report is prepared in accordance with the EIA program, the proponent or the
preparer of the EIA program, authorized by the proponent, shall make the public acquainted with
the EIA report. The same methods and procedures as during the first stage shall be employed.
12. The EIA report, the public proposals analysis, and the conclusions of the relevant parties
(subjects) of the environmental impact assessment shall be submitted to the Environmental
Protection Ministry for ratification.
13. Governmental institutions, public organizations, and other physical persons or legal entities
may appeal the public discussion procedures and a justifiable refusal to implement the public
proposals to the Environmental Protection Ministry at the latest within 15 days after the public
discussion. Governmental institutions, public organizations, and other physical persons or legal
entities have also the right to perform public environmental impact assessment.
14. Prior to the final decision regarding the proposed activity, the Environmental Protection
Ministry shall invite the public representatives listed in paragraph 13 to participate in the
consideration of public proposals and conclusions of experts.

The Government of the Republic of Lithuania
Resolution No 456 of 12 May 1997
concerning the approval of the list of proposed activities and projects that shall be made subject to
the full environmental impact assessment
Acting in accordance with the Law on Environmental Impact Assessment of the Republic of
Lithuania ("State News," 1996, No 82 - 1965) the Governrment of the Republic of Lithuania
resolves:
1. To approve the list of the categories of proposed activities and projects that shall be made
subject to the full environmental impact assessment (enclosed).
2. To set that:
2.1. The proposed activities or projects listed in the aforementioned list shall be made subject to
the full environmental impact assessment if at least one of the following criteria are met:
2.1.1. Production capacities or other indices match the values defined in the list;
2.1.2. The volume of water consumed exceeds 250 cubic metres per 24 hours;
2.1.3. The volume of waste or sewage water recharged exceeds 100 cubic metres per 24 hours;
2.1.4. The annual volume of emissions into the atmosphere exceeds 50 tonnes;
2.1.5. During the production process (except combustion and welding processes) emissions
(regardless of the volume) belonging to the I and II risk categories are emitted into the
atmosphere;
2.1.6. The annual volume of hazardous waste produced exceeds 5 tonnes;
2.2. The "Environmental Protection" section of a construction object study for the categories of
proposed activities and projects that are not subject to full EIA pursuant to paragraphs 1 and 2
above, yet do have negative effects on the environment or use natural resources, as well as for the
constructions planned to be erected on the territories of national parks and nature reserves, shall
be prepared according to the Republican Construction Standards and coordinated according to the
established order.
The Prime Minister Gedimninas Vagnorius
The Environmental Protection Minister Imantas Lazdinis

The Republic of Lithuania                         Order No 67
Ministrv of Environment                           1997 04 17
Protection                                        Vilnius
On the assessment of the effects of Klaipeda port dredging works
on fishery
Generalizing the recommendations of the Institute of Ecology and Lithuanian
Hydrobiological Society presented in the "Assessment of the effects Malk0 bay dredging works
on fishery", "Methodical quige book for assessment of the effects of Klaipeda port dredging
works on fish migration and results of ecological monitoring of Klaipeda port, seeking to
strengthen the protection of migrating fish in the Klaipeda Strait in spawning periods and
accumulate extra means for restoration and protection of these fish supplies and following the
nature Protection Ministry Regulations (article 7.4),
I hereby order:
1. To ensure that in the period of fish spawning migration (from April 1 to May 31 and
from August 16 to October 31) the port area shall be dredged (cleaned) only in case
of urgent necessity and provided that the following conditions are followed:
1.1. A plan of dredging works must be prepared and coordinated with the
Department of Fish Supplies before the beginning of the works. The plan
must contain information about concrete dredging sites, terms and range and
provide measures for reducing the negative effects on fish migration.
1.2. In the course of dredging works the port, by its own expenses must carry out
a monitoring investigation of migration intensity and dredging works effects
on migrating fish. If there is a necessity certain corrections of the dredging
works must be made in 24 hours. The investigations must be carried out by
specialists who are not subordinate to the port.              1
2. Depending on the dredged part of the port the following reimbursement prices for
damage inflicted to fish migration must be determined:
2.1. When dredging works are carried out in the western nearshore of the
Klaipeda Strait, navigation channel, monoeuvring area of the International



ferrv or western branch of Kiaules nugara isle - 0.06 Lt for 1 m3 of dredged
out sediment.
2.2. When dredging works are carried out in the eastern nearshore of the
Klaipeda Strait (head quarters of "KLASCO", "Smelte'. "Laivite", "Klaipeda
ship repair yards", "Ship building yards Baltija", "Cardboard factory",
"Closed stock company Bega", internal roadstead, Smiltyne ferry terminal) -
0.031 Lt/m3 of sediment.
2.3. When the dredging works are carried out in the Malko bay - 0.02 Lt/m3 of
sediment.
3. To ensure that in the period of intensive fish migration (from April 15 till May 15 and
from September 5 till October 15) the damage reimbursement prices will be
multiplied by coefficient 2.
4. It must be determined that violation of conditions provided in the plan (when the
indicated conditions are not kept to or when recommendations for corrections -
supported by investigation results - are not taken into account) make the dredging
works illegal and  the  executives answer   according  to  the  law. When
recommendations, sustained by results of investigation are at variance with the plan it
is necessary to keep to recommendations.
5. Using the actual investigation data the Department of Fish Supplies must specify the
dates of the beginning and end of spring and autumn migrations and duration of
intensive migration if there is such a need.
6. The reimbursement means (for damage inflicted to the process of fish migration)
must be used for protection and regeneration of fish supplies.
7. The Order must be distributed to the Department of Fish Supplies, Klaipeda Regional
department, Klaipeda State Port administration.
8. The keywords in the computer database of the Ministry of Environment Protection
are "wildlife" and "management"
Minister
I. Lazdinis



The Republic of Lithuania
Ministry of Environment Protection
Instructions for Klaipeda Port area and Sea channel dredging
(cleaning and deepening) and sediment dumping in the Sea works
1994
The Instructions were approved by the order No54 of November 16, 1994 issued by the
Department of Environment Protection
The Instructions were worked out by a team headed by prof. B.Gailiu6is to the order of
Klaipeda State Port administration.
Provisional instructions for Klaipeda Port area and Sea channel dredging and
sediment dumping in the Sea works
1. General part.
1.1. The Instructions were worked out following the convention for marine
environment in the Baltic Sea region, Low of environment protection of the
Republic of Lithuania, Regulations of the Lithuanian Ministry of
Environment Protection, HELKOM recommendations and foreign experience.
The Instructions provide the procedures and conditions for submission of
applications and issuing permissions for bottom dredging and sediment
dumping in the Sea works.



1.2. The Instructions reflect the results of scientific investigations of effects
produced by bottom dredging and sediment dumping, on the environment.
The effects are the following:
* intensification of water circulation between  the Baltic Sea and
Curonian lagoon as a result of increased hydraulic conductivity of the
Strait.
* secondarv water pollution ith toxic. c.nntaminations in the process of
sediment dredging,
* bottom deformations resulting structural changes of the speed of water
flows,
* degradation of hydrocaenoses reducing the food basis for fish, water
self-cleaning capacity and ecosystems stability,
* changes of fish migration and spawning conditions during dredging
works,
* marine water pollution by soil dumping,
* a necessity to control the mentioned works seeking to estimate their
effects on the environment and eliminate the harmful consequences.
1.3. Explanation of terms:
* "Sea" means the territorial and economic zone of the Republic of
Lithuania in the Baltic Sea and Curonian lagoon.
* "territorial waters" and "economic zone" - part of the Baltic Sea
delimited by agreements between the Republic of Lithuania and other
countries and determined by the Lithuanian Law,
* "ships" mean any type of vessels including the self-propelled and
tugged ones, ships on air cushion and with hydrofoils, submarines,
stationary and floating platforms,
* "bottom dredging for deepening purposes" (bottom deepening) is an
increase of the project depth or width of port area.
* "bottom dredging for cleaning purposes" (bottom cleaning) is removal
of bottom sediments seeking to restore the project depth or width of
port area.
* "dumping" means sediment disposal from a ship,
* "client" means Klaipeda Port administration or port enterprise
exploiting part of the port,



* "contractor" means: a) enterprise which implements the dredging
work by contract, b) vessel carrying the dredged out sediment,
* "sediment" - surface sediments or rock of the Sea bottom,
* "aleurite" - 0.01 - 0.00 1 mm sediment particles,
1.4. The Instructions are applied for licenced (permitted) dredging and dumping
works. Dumping in the Sea of any other materials and wastes, as well as ships
or aircrarfs is prorhibited.
2. Conditions of dredging works:
2.1. The character of dredging works depends on their purpose. There are two
kinds of dredging works - bottom dredging for cleaning and bottom dredging
for deepening purposes.
2.2. In periods of intensive valuable fish migration (April 1 - May 31, August 16
- October 31) bottom dredging works are limited. Limiting conditions can be
found in an issued permission.
2.3. A project for bottom dredging works must contain a chapter on nature
protection providing measures for nature protection.
2.4. According to the intensity of Klaipeda Strait bottom processes the whole
aquatory is divided into three sectors with indicated exploitation depths of
fair ways (Supplement No l.of the Instruction). The scheme also contains
recommended exploitation depths for each port area. While carrying out
dredging works these depths should be taken into consideration (see Table 1.).
2.5. Toxicants characteristic of the region are most widely spread in the bottom
sediments of port area and Sea channel : chromium, nickel, copper, lead,
mercury, cadmium, zinc, oil products (Supplements 2 and 3). According to
the concentration of these chemicals in the bottom sediments the latter are
grouped in four pollution classes (Table 2). The class of sediment pollution is
determined providing that MCL of no toxicant is exceeded.
2.6. The sediments of class 1 and 2 (clean and little polluted) may be dumped in
the Sea or used for leveling of the territory, road building, ect.
2.7. The sediments of class 3 and 4 may be dumped in the Sea only in
exceptional cases when the content of (Table 2) mobile forms of heavy
metals,  pesticides,  phenols,  polychorbiphenils,  benz(a)pyrene  and
radionuclides is determined, hypothesis of effects on the environment worked
)



out and other ways of sediment detoxication and use were considered and
rejected.
2.8. Polluted and highly polluted sediments (class 3 and 4) on which a
permission for dumping in the Sea was not given, are transported to landfill or
other utilization site coordinated with the Ministry of Environment Protection
2.9. The level of port area and Sea channel bottom sediments pollution is
determined:
* in loams and sands - no less than once in the three years,
* in aleurites and sands with aleurites - every time before applying for
permission to implement dredging works.
2.10. Permissions for dredging works are issued on the ground of investigation
results of the following number of sediment samples (depending on the
planned quantity of sediments):
3 - when the planned quantity of dredged sediments is 25 000 m3.
4-6 - from 25 000 to 100 000 m3
7 - 15 - from lOO 000 to 500 000 m3
16-30-from500000to2000000m3
2.11. Monitoring of dredging works in the port area represents repeated
investigations of the parameters of marine environment and control of
mediate and immediate effects on the environment. The monitoring is
implemented by the Klaipeda Port Administration within the framework of
the programme cordinated with the Ministry of Environment protection.
Sediment and water samples should be analysed by authorized laboratories.
3. Procedures for getting a permission for dredging works.
3.1 Free formn applications for bottom dredging and sediment dumping works are
to be submitted to the Klaipeda Port Administration. The client must prepare
a permission project following the requirements (Supplement 4). Head of the
client enterprise is responsible for reliability of data in the permission project.
The Klaipeda State Port submits the material for getting a permission to the
Ministry of the Environment Protection.
3.2 The permission for port area dredging is issued after a submission to the
Ministry of Environment Protection of the following: 1) project task,



coordinated with involved organizations, of a new  building  or new
(reconstructed) port area construction, 2) hypothesis of effects of projected
dredging works, 3) project of nature protection measures to reduce the
harnfull effects. The Ministry of Environment Protection carries out an
ecological expertise of construction or reconstruction works on the ground of
submitted and any other information. A positive conclusion on project
doincumenation is at the samne timne a permission to carry out dredging works.
3.3 The application for permission to carry out bottom dredging and sediment
dumping works must be submited by the Klaipeda Port Administration to the
Klaipeda Regional Department of MEP in a special form (Supplement 4) and
45 days before the beginning of works. The permission must be issued (or a
written refusal to issue) in 30 days from the data of submission of material.
Three copies of permission must be distributed (to client, Port administration,
and Klaipeda Regional Department of MEP).
3.4 Under special conditions of exploitation, when the depth and width of the
Port area suddenly change as a result of storms, tides, landslips and other
elemental forces, the Klaipeda Regional department of MEP may issue a
permission for dredging and dumping works in the order of emergency. The
emergency permission is issued in three days after a submission of free form
application and bathymetric plan with a description of projected works.
3.5 The client submits an account of implemented works to the Klaipeda Port
Administration and Klaipeda Regional Department of MEP every quarter of
the year and after a completion of the work. After the completion of the work
the client submits a bathymetric plan of area in which the dredging works
were carried out. The client is allowed to begin the exploitation of the dredged
area only after a permission from the Klaipeda Port Administration.
3.6 The Klaipeda Regional Department of MEP does the registration of
sediments to be dumped in the Sea (quantity, kind, locality, time and
methods) on the ground of client's accounts.
3.7 The permission for bottom dredging and sediment dumping works is issued
in the client's name. In case of violation of conditions provided in the
permission or unexpected environmental pollution for executive's fault the
perpetrator answers according to the Law.

L    VMIRODUCTION
The objective of this study was to examine the toxicological properties of sediment from
Klaipeda, Lithuania.
Whole sediment toxicity of the nine samples from Klaipeda were assessed through 10-day
exposures with the amrphipod, Eohaustorius estuarius.
1L    TEST ADMIN-ISTRATION
A.    Sponsor
Frederic R. Harris B.V.

2587 CA Den Haag
The Netherlands

Flemington, New Jersey 08822

m. MATERIALS AND METHODS
All testing was performed in accordance with ASTM. 1992. Guide for Conducting 10 -Day
Static Sediment Toxicity Tests with Marine and Estuarine Amphipods, E1367-92. American
Society for Testing and Materials, Philadelphia.
499 Point Breeze Road / Flemingron, NJ 08822
FI n    Phone: 908/788-8700  Fax: 908/788-9165 E-mail; aquasurvey@aol.com  Web Site: www.aquasurvey.com



Aqua Survey, Inc
A.    Sampling
Test sediment from the nine locations was collected by the sponsor. The samples
were received in good condition at ASI in Flemington, NJ, and stored in the dark at
4C. Upon arrival at ASI, all samples were logged in and assigned a unique sample
number. Sample identification numbers are listed below:
BH-A                 90859
BH-B                 90860
BH-D                 90861
BH-E                 90862
BH-F                 90863
BH-G                 90864
BH-I                 90865
BH-J                 90866
BH-K                 90867
Control sediment used in the solid phase testing with E. estuarius was obtained from
the site of organism collection and was provided along with the organisms from
Northwestern Aquatic Sciences, Newport, Oregon.
Manasquan Water, obtained from Manasquan Inlet, New Jersey, was used as the
overlay water. This water was tested according to ASTM guidelines to ensure its
purity. The results of water analysis and sample receiving logs for Manasquan Water
are included in the appendix.
4
499 Point Breeze Road / Flemington, NJ 08822
Y1    Phone: 908/788-8700  Fax: 908/788-9165 E-mail: aquasurvey@aol-com  Web Sire: wwwaquasurvey.com



Aqua Survey, Inc.
B.    Solid Phase Testing
Whole sediment toxicity of the nine samples was assessed through 1 0-day exposures
with the amphipod, E. estuiarius. The organisn, E. esturarius used in testing were
3-5 mm in size. They were received on May 5, 1999 and were held for two days
before test initiation, during which time they were acclimated to test salinity (20 - 2
ppt) and temperature (15  2 C).
Some of the samples were extremely sandy, consequently we were unable to ooiain
sufficient porewater to enable us to do ammonia measurements. Only one sample,
BH-E (ASI 490862) produced enough pore water for ammonia determination, this
was 18.8 mg/L. As this sample was below the 20 mg/L threshold suggested by
USEPA guidance, ammonia purging was not required and the testing on all samples
were conducted following a static non-renewal methodology.
The day before test initiation, five replicates of 175 rml of each sediment was set out
in 1-Liter Tripours. To each Tripour, 725 mL of Manasquan Water was carefully
added to minirnize the disturbance of the sediment All chambers were aerated to
ensure that the dissolved oxygen was maintained at greater than 90% saturation. The
sediment was allowed to settle overnight. Before the addition of the organism, E.
estuarius to the exposure chambers, water quality parameters (pH, temperature,
salinity and DO) were measured in the overlay water. Each chamber was stocked with
20 organisms. Testing was conducted in continuous light, - 500-1000 lux. Daily
water quality parameters were measured along with the total ammonia in one replicate
from each sample. Observations of the test organisms were also made daily.
After ten days of exposure to the nine sediment samples from Klaipeda, live count
data from the solid phase test was entered into a spreadsheet, sorted and tabulated.
A Standard Reference Toxicant test was performed and reference toxicant data were
entered into a program based on currently accepted methods for calculating an LC50.
A control chart can be found in the appendix.
5
0fX                          499 Point Breeze Road / Flemington, NJ 08822
Phone: 908/788-8700  Fax: 908/788-9165 E-mail: aquasurvey@aol.com  Web Site: www.aquasurvey.com



Aqua Survey, Inc.
IV.   RESULTS A1ND DISCUSSION
Test results as well as water quality parameters are summarized in the tables at the end of this
report. Raw data for biological effects and water quality parameters are presented in the
Appendix.
A.    Solid Phase Testing
After ten days, E. estuarius exposed to the nine samples of sediment from Klaipeda,
Lithuania did not show a statistically significant reduction in survival when compared
to the survival of organisms in the control. Normally the statistical comparison is
made to a reference sample, but in its absence the control was used as the basis for
comparison. In accordance with the 1991 USEPA guidance for dredged sediment
testing projects, samples are considered toxic if survival of organisms exposed to test
sediment are at least 20% less than the survival observed in the reference sediment
and this difference is statistically signficant (p<0.05) after a ten-day test period. These
results indicate that sample BH-I is statistically significant when compared to the
control however, since survival in this sarnple was within 20% of the control it is not
considered toxic under USEPA guidelines. No other samples were statistically
significant.
